824	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Akteruddin Master alias Aftabuddin and others Vs.  The State (Syed Md. Ziaul Karim, J.)</h2>

Shorwardhi, A.A.G.,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2020(1) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2014</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Akteruddin Master alias Aftabuddin and others</p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  The State</p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Words and Phrases</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-07-13</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 10.5pt; line-height: 150%;">(CRIMINAL APPELLATE JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 6.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 106.0pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top" width="141"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.4pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold','serif'; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Syed Md. Zakir Hossain, J</strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></p></td><td style="width: 94.05pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Akteruddin Master alias Aftabuddin and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Informant-appellant</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The State</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Respondent</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> </span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Words and Phrases</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Charge</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">A charge is defined as a ‘precise’ formulation of the specific accusation made against a person who is entitled to know its nature at the very earliest stage. ...(11)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 242</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">We should bear in mind, credibility of testimony oral and circumstantial, depends considerably on a judicial evaluation of the totality, not isolated scrutiny. When dealing with the serious question of guilt or innocence of persons charged with crime, the following principles should be taken into consideration.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">a) The onus of proving everything essential to the establishment of the charge against the accused lies on the prosecutor.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">b) The evidence must be such asto exclude to a moral certainty every reasonable doubt of the guilt of the accused.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">c) In matters of doubt it is safer to acquit than to condemn, for it is better that several guilty persons should escape than that one innocent person suffer.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">d) There must be clear and unequivocal proof of the corpus delicit.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">e) The hypothesis of delinquency should be consistent with all the facts proved.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">In spite of the presumption of truth attached to oral evidence under oath if the Court is not satisfied, the evidence in spite of oath is of no avail.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                </span>...(9)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Sections 173, 202 and 242</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">“Charge” corresponds to an “indictment” in English Law and is very much more than a mere form. It is a precise formulation of specific accusation made against a person. Charge has to be framed on the basis of the material placed before the Trial Court and while doing so the Court is not bound by the inquiry report submitted under section 202 of the Code of Criminal Procedure or in a Police Challan case by the report submitted under section 173 of the Code of Criminal Procedure. Conditions for framing of a charge are (i) presumption of the commission of an offence on the materials before the Court and (ii) offences triable exclusively by a competent Court.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                 </span>...(11 and 13)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 242</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishes Bidhan) Ain (XVIII of <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">1995)</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Sections 9©, 6(1) and 14</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">All that is required at the stage of framing charge is to see whether the prima-facie case regarding commission of certain offence is made out. The truth veracity and effect of evidence which prosecution propose to adduce at the time is not to be meticulously judged at the stage of framing charge. The offence punishable under sections 9©, 6(1) and 14 of the Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishes Bidhan) Ain, 1995 have been clearly disclosed in the instant case against the appellants. We have gone through the grounds taken in the petition of appeal and we find that such grounds are absolutely the disputed question of facts and the same should be decided at trial. The plea of the appellants is nothing but the defence plea. Be that as it may the proposition of law is now well settled that on the basis of defence plea or materials the criminal proceedings should not be stifled before trial; when there is a prima-facie case for going for trial. in view of such facts the grounds taken the petition of appeal are not the correct exposition of law.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                </span>...(15)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Mohd. Aquil and another Vs. The state 1988 Crl. L.J. 1484 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                                      </span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">No one appears</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: right; line-height: 110%;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">For Informant-appellant</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mrs. Sakila Rowshan,D.A.G. with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mrs. Sharmina Haque, A.A.G. and</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> Md.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> Shorwardhi, A.A.G.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">For the State-respondent</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="text-decoration: none;"> </span></span></u></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="text-decoration: none;"> </span></span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Syed Md. Ziaul Karim, J. </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">By this appeal, accused-appellants have challenged the legality and propriety of the order dated 19-08-1999 passed by learned Judge of Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Daman Bishes Adalat, Gaibandha ( briefly as Adalat) framing charge under Sections 9(c), 6((1), 14 of the Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishes Bidhan) Ain, 1995( briefly as Ain, 1995) in Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Case no. 65 of 1999.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Facts in brief are that on 16-02-1999 Most. Lucky Khatun as complainant filed a petition of complaint in the Court of Magistrate, first Class, Gaibandha against the accused appellants alleging that she was a student of H.S.C. of Belka Colleege and accused no.1 Titu Mia was a student of B.A. at Sundarganj College. An intimacy developed between them on they way to college. Due to such intimacy the accused consecutively committed rape upon her at the instance of other co-accused. Consequently she repeatedly requested the accused for marriage<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>but with no effect. With these allegations she lodged the instance case. Later, the case was referred to the Police Station wherein it was recorded<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>as Sundargonj Police Station case no.02 dated 01-03-1999 under sections 6(1), 9( c), and 14 of the Ain, 1995.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Police after investigation submitted charge-sheet accusing the accused Titu Mia and submitted final report in favour of the other co-accused.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On receipt of the Police report, the learned Magistrate, referred the case to the Adalat for trial wherein the cognizance was taken under the aforesaid sections and eventually charge was framed under sections 9(c), 6(1) and 14 of the Ain, 1995 by the impugned order.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Feeling aggrieved the appellants preferred the instant appeal.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">No one appears on behalf of the appellants to press the appeal. In view of the facts, this is an old appeal of 1999 we are inclined to take it up for disposal on merit considering the materials on record. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Deputy Attorney General appearing for the State-respondent opposes the appeal and submits that after considering the materials on record the learned Judge of the Court below rightly framed charge which calls for no interference by this Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In order to appreciate her submissions we have gone through the record and given our anxious consideration to her submissions.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">We should bear in mind, credibility of testimony oral and circumstantial, depends considerably on a judicial evaluation of the totality, not isolated scrutiny. When dealing with the serious question of guilt or innocence of persons charged with crime, the following principles should be taken into consideration. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .75in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">a) The onus of proving everything essential to the establishment of the charge against the accused lies on the prosecutor.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .75in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">b)<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>The evidence must be such asto exclude to a moral certainty every reasonable doubt of the guilt of the accused.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .75in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">c)<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>In matters of doubt it is safer to acquit than to condemn, for it is better that several guilty persons should escape than that one innocent person suffer.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .75in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">d) There must be clear and unequivocal proof of the corpus delicit.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .75in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">e)<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>The hypothesis of delinquency should be consistent with all the facts proved.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .25in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Inspite of the presumption of truth attached to oral evidence under oath if the Court is not satisfied, the evidence inspite of oath is of no avail.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">A "Charge" corresponds to an "indictment" in English Law and is very much more than a mere form. It is a precise formulation of specific accusation made against a person. Charge has to be framed on the basis of the material placed before the Trial Court and while doing so the Court is not bound by the inquiry report submitted under section 202 of the Code of Criminal Procedure or in a Police challan case by the report submitted under section 173 of the Code of Criminal Procedure.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">A charge is an important step in a criminal proceeding. It separates the inquiry stage from trial. The whole object of framing a charge is to enable the defence to concentrate its attention on the case that he has to meet, and if charge is framed in such a vague manner that the necessary ingredients of the offence with which the accused is convicted are not brought out in the charge, then the charge is defective. The framing of a proper charge is vital to a criminal trial and this is a matter on which the Magistrate or Judge should bestow the most careful attention. A charge should be carefully drawn up in accordance with the offence disclosed. The charge should be precise in its scope and particular in its details. A charge is defined as a ‘precise formulation of the specific accusation made against a person who is entitled to know its nature at the very earliest stage. The necessity of a system of written accusation specifying a definite criminal offence is the essence of criminal procedure.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The charge-sheet to which the accused is called upon to plead is a very important document. It should be drawn up and considered with extreme care and caution, so that accused may have no doubt whatever as to the offences to which he is called upon to answer and the Judge of the Appellate Court also may have no doubt upon the matter. The word ‘Ground’ means basis, foundation or valid reason. The whole object of framing a charge is to enable the defence to concentrate its attention on the case that he has to meet. Conditions for framing of a charge are (i) presumption of the commission of an offence on the materials before the Court and (ii) offences triable exclusively by a competent Court.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of Mohd. Aqil and another Vs. The State 1988 Crl. L.J. 1484 held:</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 1.0in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">            </span>"Framing of charge- Matters to be considered by Court indicated.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 1.0in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">            </span>For the purpose of framing a charge the Court is required to consider judicially asto whether on consideration of the materials on record, it can be said that the accused has reasonably connected himself with the offence alleged to have been committed and that on the basis of the said material there is reasonable probability or chance of the accused<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>being found guilty of the offence alleged. If the answer is in the affirmative, the Court will be at liberty to presume "that the accused has committed the offence” as mentioned in S. 228 for the purpose of framing<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the charge. In finding out a prima-facie case not only the F.I.R. or complaint but even the statements of the witnesses recorded under S. 161 although the same may have been recorded after some delay during the investigation of the case are to be taken into consideration and if from all other material, a prima facie case is made out against the accused then the Magistrate has no option but to frame a charge against the accused. The Court is not expected to make a roving enquiry in the pros and cons of the matter and weigh the evidence as if he was conducting a trial. However, in a case, if two views are possible and the Judge is satisfied that evidence produced before him while giving rise to some suspicion does not give rise to grave suspicion against the accused, he will<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>be fully within his right to discharge the accused."</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 1.0in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><strong style="text-indent: 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">2.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></strong><span style="text-indent: 0in; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">On going to the materials on record it transpires that the informant categorically narrated the manner of crime committed by the accused. The learned Judge after considering the entire materials on record rightly framed charge under sections 9(c) 6(1), 14 of the Ain,1995 against the appellants. All that is required at the stage of framing charge is to see whether the prima-facie case regarding commission of certain offence is made out. The truth veracity and effect of evidence which prosecution proposes to adduce at the time is not to be meticulously judged at the stage of framing charge. In the instant case the accused stand indicted for offence punishable under sections 9(c) 6(1), 14 of the Ain,1995. Cognizance has been taken under the said sections. We have meticulously examined the </span><span style="font-size: 11pt;">allegations made by the informant and we find that the offence punishable under sections 9(c) 6(1), 14 of the Ain,1995 have been clearly disclosed in the instant case against the appellants. We have gone through the grounds taken in the petition of appeal and we find that such grounds are absolutely the disputed question of facts and the same should be decided at trial. The plea of the appellants are nothing but the defence plea. Be that as it may the proposition of law is now well settled that on the basis of defence plea or materials the criminal proceedings should not be stifled before trial; when there is a prima-facie case for going for trial. In view of such facts the grounds taken in the petition of appeal are not the correct exposition of law. Moreso interruption of the course of Justice will set up a wrong precedent by which the course of justice instead of being advanced readily been stifled inasmuchas the grounds advanced before us are not correct or legal exposition of law. Therefore we hold that there are sufficient grounds for proceeding against the appellants for going for trial under sections 9(c) 6(1), 14 of the Ain,1995. To that end in view we are at one with the learned Judge of the Court below regarding framing of charge against the appellants. In view of the above we failed to discover any merit in this appeal. Thus the appeal having no merit fails.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">16.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of foregoing narrative the appeal is dismissed. The order of stay granted earlier stands vacated.          </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">17.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Office is directed to communicate the order at once.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"> </p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///C:/Users/Hp/Downloads/masum/Issue_January_2020(1)/Issue%20__January__2020(1)_Cr.%20A.%20No.1995%20of%2099_Md.%20Ziaul%20Karim,%20J.__6.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><u></u></a></p></div></div></div></div>
825	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Aminul Islam Chowdhury Vs. Abdul Sukkur Sarker and others (Muha. Imman Ali, J.)  </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL  APPEAL  NO. 598 OF  2009  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Muhammad Imman Ali, J Mirza Hussain Haider, J      And Abu Bakar Siddiquee, J, </p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Abdul Wadud Bhuiyan Senior Advocate, instructed by Syed Mahbubar Rahman Advocate-on-Record,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2020(1) LNJ (AD) </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Aminul Islam Chowdhury </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Abdul Sukkur Sarker and others </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Waqfs Ordinance (I of 1962)</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-07-13</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">Mirza Hussain Haider</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;
