margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">15-05-2019</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 15.95pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 115.6pt;" width="21"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///C:/Users/Hp/Downloads/masum/Issue_January_2020(1)%201/Issue__January_20(1)__C.%20A.%20598%20%20of%202009__Muhammad%20Imman%20Ali_J___AD___2.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 92.2pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 115.6pt;" width="123"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Aminul Islam Chowdhury</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . . </span></strong><strong><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN-GB;">Appellants</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Abdul Sukkur Sarker and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . Respondents.</span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">Waqfs Ordinance (I of 1962)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Sections 56 and 57</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Property belonging to a Waqf may only be transferred by its Mutawalli after getting sanction from the Administrator of Waqfs, as provided by section 57 read with section 56 of the Waqfs Ordinance, 1962. 16</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">Waqfs Ordinance (I of 1962)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">Sections 56(3)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Any transfer made by a Mutawalli without the sanction from the Administrator of Waqfs shall be declared void, if the Administrator, within 4 months of his coming to know of such transfer, or within 3 years from the date of such transfer, whichever is later, applies to the Civil Court in this behalf. Thus, it is solely in the domain of the Administrator of Waqfs to challenge any transfer of Waqf property by a Mutawalli.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">       </span>16</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">Waqfs Ordinance (I of 1962)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">Sections 102</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The finding of the Administrator of WEaqfs of the effect that the predecessor of the appellant-plaintiff in the suit had consented to the transfer of the property in question is a finding of fact which could have been agitated by the plaintiff in a properly constituted case challenge before the concerned District Judge. But he did not do so. Hence, the finding that the transfer was valid cannot be challenged by him since there is a bar under section 102 of the Ordinance.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                </span>17</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt; mso-ansi-language: EN-GB;">For the Appellants</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt;">: </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Abdul Wadud Bhuiyan Senior Advocate, instructed by Syed Mahbubar Rahman Advocate-on-Record</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">For the Respondent No.2-9</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">: Mr. Abdul Quayum Senior Advocate, instructed by Mr. Zainul Abedin Advocate –on-Record </span><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN-GB; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Respondent Nos.2-8: None represented</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">For the Respondent No.1&amp;10</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">: None represented</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">JUDGMENT</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><u><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps; mso-ansi-language: EN-GB;">MUHAMMAD IMMAN ALI</span></u></strong><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">This civil appeal, by leave, is directed against the judgement and order dated 14.05.2008 passed by a Single </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Bench of the High Court Division in Civil Revision No.443 of 2001 discharging the Rule. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                  </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The facts of the case, in short, are that Zaker Ali Sowdagar was the owner of the land described in the schedule to the plaint and he made a waqf in respect of the property together with his other properties by executing and registering a waqf deed dated 10.05.1928 as Waqf Alal Aulad conferring benefits to the cause of religion, charity and his heirs. The Waqf Estate was duly registered with the Administrator of Waqfs-defendant No.10 bearing E.C. No.7035 and the schedule-1 property has been mentioned in item No.40 of the said waqf deed. The waqif Zaker Ali Sowdagar constituted himself as the first Mutawalli and he acted as such and managed and possessed the waqf properties within the terms and conditions of the said waqf deed till his death. After his death his first son late Imam Sharif Chowdhury became the Mutawalli of his Waqf Estate and he managed the same till his death. After his death the wakif’s second son Md. Sharif Chowdhury became the Mutawalli and his grandson the plaintiff Alhaj Nurul Islam Chowdhury son of late Imam Sharif Chowdhury became the Naib Mutawalli of the said Waqf Estate. Both of them used to manage the Waqf Estate jointly but by amicable partition Mutawalli Md. Sharif Chowdhury used to possess half of the entire Waqf Estate and the rest used to be possessed by the plaintiff. As per amicable partition, schedule-1(a) property was in possession of Mutawalli Md. Sharif Chowdhury and the rest of the schedule property was in possession of the plaintiff. The administration and management of the entire Waqf Estate was entrusted to the joint management of the plaintiff and Md. Sharif Chowdhury. The said Mutawalli Md. Sharif Chowdhury having died in June, 1979 the plaintiff became the sole Mutawalli of the said Waqf Estate and defendant No.10-the Administrator of Waqfs also has appointed the plaintiff as sole Mutawalli by his Memo No.1413 dated 10.12.1979 and since then the plaintiff has been managing the waqf property. Md. Sharif Chowdhury and the plaintiff were also the beneficiaries of the entire Waqf Estate and P.S. and B.S. Khatians have been recorded in their names for the purpose of enjoyment of the usufruct of the Waqf Estate as beneficiaries. Md. Sharif Chowdhury was in possession of the schedule-1(a) property in the eastern part of the schedule-1 property covered by municipal holding No.92 old and 95 new, house No.294 and the plaintiff was in possession of the remaining western part of the schedule property covered by municipal holding No.91 old and 94 new, house No.295. Md. Sharif Chowdhury as Mutawalli illegally transferred the schedule-1(a) property to defendant Nos.1 to 9 by 3 registered kabalas dated 19.03.1977, 20.03.1977 and 22.03.1977 bearing deed Nos.3063, 3012 and 3036. The<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>plaintiff having come to know of the fact of the transfers made a complaint before defendant No.10-the Administrator of Waqfs requesting him to recover possession of the schedule-1(a) property from defendant Nos.1 to 9 by a petition, whereupon the Administrator of Waqfs filed Miscellaneous Case No.208 of 1981 in the First Court of Subordinate Judge, Chattogram under section 56(3) of the Waqf Ordinance, 1962 (the Ordinance) on 03.06.1981 against defendant Nos.1 to 9 for recovery of possession. In that miscellaneous case the Administrator of Waqfs clearly stated that Mutawalli Md. Sharif Chowdhury did not take permission from the Administrator of Waqfs for transferring the schedule 1(a) property to defendant Nos.1 to 9 and the alleged kabalas are fraudulent and illegal and the transferees did not acquire any title and interest in the schedule-1(a) property and the kabalas are liable to be declared void and illegal and the schedule-1(a) property is liable to be recovered from defendant Nos.1 to 9.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                  </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Defendant Nos.1 to 9 without appearing in the miscellaneous case filed a petition before the Administrator of Waqfs on 26.09.1981 and prevailed upon him illegally to recognise their purchase and to pass illegal order on 04.02.1982 according permission to the aforesaid transfers with retrospective effect and to direct the local Waqfs Inspector to withdraw the Miscellaneous Case No.208 of 1981 from the Court of Subordinate Judge, First Court, Chattogram. On the petition filed by the Administrator of Waqfs for withdrawal of the Miscellaneous Case No.208 of 1981 the learned Subordinate Judge, Second Court-in-charge of the First Court rejected the objection of the plaintiff who was opposite party No.10 in the miscellaneous case and allowed the withdrawal of the petition in Miscellaneous Case No.208 of 1981 by order dated 18.02.1982. On the same date the plaintiff’s application to be added as co-petitioner in the said miscellaneous case was also rejected. Hence, the plaintiff filed the suit for declaration and recovery of possession.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                  </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Defendant No.l contested the suit by filing written statement denying the allegations of the plaintiff contending, <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">inter alia,</em> that defendant No.1 had to file a petition before the Administrator of Waqfs-defendant No.10 praying for withdrawal of the Miscellaneous Case No.208 of 1981 when defendants were convinced that the plaintiff had manipulated the Administrator of Waqfs to file the miscellaneous case knowing full well that the defendants obtained kabalas from the Mutawalli who obtained permission from defendant No.10 for such transfers with the consent of the plaintiff. The plaintiff filed a petition before defendant No.10 after the death of the Mutawalli Md. Sharif Chowdhury, who transferred the schedule-1(a) property along with other properties in total measuring 25 decimals land, in order to make illegal gain, but by order dated 04.02.1982 defendant No.10 rejected the plaintiff’s prayer and passed order conferring the permission to transfer with retrospective effect and got the Miscellaneous Case No.208 of 1981 withdrawn. Defendant No.1 purchased 25 decimals land out of schedule-1 property in his name as well as in the names of his sons defendant Nos.2-9 to the knowledge of all concerned and possession was delivered to him. In fact he was already in possession from before as bharatia under the Mutawalli and is a <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide</em> purchaser for valuable consideration. Defendant No.10 was pleased to accord permission with retrospective effect for the transfer to meet the ends of justice directing withdrawal of the Miscellaneous Case No.208 of 1981. The suit of the plaintiff is not maintainable and it is liable to be dismissed with cost.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                  </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">On conclusion of the trial, the learned Subordinate Judge, First Court, Chattogram by his judgement and order dated 30.09.1989 dismissed the suit. Then the plaintiff preferred Other Class Appeal No.581 of 1989 before the District Judge, Chattogram.</span><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN-GB; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> On transfer the appeal was heard by the learned Additional District Judge, First Court, Chattogram, who by his judgement and order dated 28.09.2000 dismissed the appeal affirming the judgement and order passed by the trial Court. Being aggrieved, the plaintiff filed Civil Revision No.443 of 2001 before the High Court Division and obtained Rule, which upon hearing the parties was discharged. Hence, the plaintiff filed Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No.2310 of 2008 and leave was granted to consider the following grounds: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">“I. That the sale of the waqf property on 22.03.1977 by the predecessor Mutawalli without obtaining previous sanction of the Administrator of Waqfs under the mandatory provision of section 56(1) of the Ordinance was invalid in law and that the Administrator of Waqfs having filed the Miscellaneous Case No.208 of 1981 under section 56(3) of the Ordinance, for declaring the said sale as void and having thereafter passed order on 04.02.1982 giving sanction with retrospective effect to the said sale and withdrawing the Miscellaneous Case No.208 of 1981 acted arbitrarily and without jurisdiction and as such, the civil Court has jurisdiction to entertain the plaintiff’s suit to examine whether the said sale of the waqf property has been made upon following<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the provisions of the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Ordinance and whether the Administrator of Waqfs has been vested with any power to pass any order giving retrospective sanction validating an invalid transfer of waqf property under the provisions of the Ordinance, 1962.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">II. That Miscellaneous Case No.208 of 1981 under section 56(3) of the Ordinance beyond time was not maintainable as such the plaintiff’s suit is not barred under section 102 of the Waqfs Ordinance as such the High Court Division erred in law in considering this aspect of this matter.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                  </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Abdul Wadud Bhuiyan, learned Senior Advocate appearing on behalf of the appellant made submissions in line with the grounds upon which leave was granted. He further submitted that the High Court Division committed gross error of law in not holding that the Administrator of Waqfs has not been vested with any jurisdiction or power under the Ordinance to pass any order giving retrospective sanction validating an invalid transfer of waqf property under section 56 of the Ordinance.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                  </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Abdul Quayum, learned Senior Advocate appearing for respondent Nos.2-9 made submissions in support of the impugned judgement and order of the High Court Division. He also submitted that the plaintiff-appellant consented to the sale by the erstwhile Mutawalli as such now he is estopped from challenging the sale and hence the Courts below as well as the High Court Division rightly dismissed the suit. He also submitted that the plaintiff having not challenged the order rejecting his prayer for being added as co-petitioner in Miscellaneous Case No.208 of 1981 as such the present suit at his instance is not maintainable since he was party in the suit. The learned Advocate submitted that the Administrator of Waqfs gave permission to sell with retrospective effect on 03.08.1982 for reasons mentioned in Exhibit-B(1) and since Exhibit-B gives impression of sale permission to a man of ordinary prudence, and accordingly withdrawal of Miscellaneous Case No.208 of 1981 filed under section 56(3) of the Waqfs Ordinance on false representation of the plaintiff was lawful and as such the Courts below and the High Court Division rightly dismissed the suit. He submitted that under section 56(3) of the Waqfs Ordinance it is the Administrator of Waqfs and not of any private person who may challenge the transfer of any Waqf property and the Administrator of Waqfs has exercised his right by filing Miscellaneous Case No.208 of 1981 and all are bound by the result and legal effect of the said case. He submitted that the plaintiff in the context of the case has no <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">locus standi</em> to file the suit as such the Courts below rightly dismissed the suit. The learned Advocate lastly submitted that the High Court Division rightly held that the suit is barred under section 102 of the Ordinance.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                  </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">We have considered the submissions of the learned Advocates appearing for the parties concerned, perused the impugned judgement and order of the High Court Division and other connected papers on record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                  </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">It is an admitted fact that the suit land belonged to a duly registered Waqf Estate, EC No.7035 created by late Zaker Ali Sowdagar by a deed of Waqf dated 10.5.1928. Late Alhaj Nurul Islam, the predecessor of the present appellant was a co-Mutawalli along with Md. Sharif Chowdhury. Each Mutawalli was in possession of half of the Waqf Estate. Md. Sharif Chowdhury sold 25 decimals land of his share of the Waqf Estate by three registered deeds dated 19.03.77, 20.03.77 and 22.03.77 in favour of respondent Nos.1–9. The predecessor of the present appellant filed Other Suit No.60 of 1982 praying for a declaration that the said three deeds were null and void, without proper consideration, inoperative, ineffective, sham paper transaction, without any legal consequence and not binding either upon the schedule-1(a) properties or the plaintiff. In addition he prayed for recovery of possession of the schedule-1(a) property.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">              </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The aforementioned suit was dismissed by the trial court upon finding that the plaintiff did not have <em>locus standi </em>to file the suit as there is a bar under section 102 of the Waqfs Ordinance. The learned Judge of the trial Court noted that the plaint shows cause of action on 21.03.1977 when the deeds were registered, and subsequently when defendant No.10 by order dated 04.02.1982 accorded permission with retrospective effect for sale of the schedule-1(a) property and on 18.02.1982 when the Miscellaneous Case No.208 of 1981 was withdrawn. It appeared to the learned Judge of the trial Court that the plaintiff’s challenge was against the orders of defendant No.10 (the Administrator of Waqfs) dated 4.2.82 and 18.2.82, which he could have challenged before the learned District Judge. It was further observed, by reference to exhibit-B(1) that the plaintiff consented to transfer such land in favour of defendant Nos.1-9.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">              </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The appellate Court dismissed the appeal taking a similar view as the trial Court. The appellate Court observed as follows </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">""fËcne£Ñ-¢h (1) cª­ø ­cM¡ ¢Nu¡­R ®k e¡¢mn£ pÇf¢š qÙ¹¡¿¹­ll hÉ¡f¡­l h¡c£ ¢m¢Mai¡­h pÇj¢a ‘¡fe L¢lu¡¢R­mez''</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> The learned judge observed that the plaintiff filed the instant suit having been aggrieved by the order of the Administrator of Waqfs dated 04.02.82, which is barred under section 102 of the Waqfs Ordinance, 1962. The High Court Division took the same view in discharging the Rule, which had been obtained by the appellant upon challenging the judgement and decree of the appellate Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">              </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">We find from the records that upon the death of Md. Sharif Chowdhury, by order dated 10.12.1979 the plaintiff Hazi Nurul Islam Chowdhury was appointed sole Mutawalli for the Waqf Estate. However, before his death Md. Sharif Chowdhury transferred 25 decimals land having obtained permission from the Administrator of Waqfs. We also find from the records that the previous Mutawalli, Md. Sharif Chowdhury, by an application dated 28.07.1976 sought permission from the Administrator of Waqfs to sell a portion of the Waqf property in order to meet cost of maintenance and other expenses of the Waqf property. In due course a letter was issued on 14.3.77 which was signed on behalf of the Administrator of Waqfs. The contents of the said letter are as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .25in; text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">""¢Sm¡x QVÊÊNË¡jz </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">a¡q¡l ®fË¢la 28/8/76 Cw a¡¢l­Ml clM¡­Ù¹l f¢l­fË¢r­a J ÙÛ¡e£u Ju¡Lg f¢lcnÑ­Ll ac¿¹ ¢hhlZ£l f¢l­fË¢r­a <u>Ju¡Lg pÇf¢š ¢hœ²u L¢lu¡ ¢hœ²umì V¡L¡ ¢cu¡ ¢L ¢L L¡­S La V¡L¡ hÉu L¢lu¡­Re</u> a¡q¡ BN¡j£ 25/4/76Cw a¡¢l­Ml j­dÉ c¡¢Mm L¢l­hez </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">            </span><u>¢h¢œ²a</u> pÇf¢šl af¢Rmz </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">­Sm¡x QVÊNË¡j, ®j±S¡ f¡blL¡V¡, 34609 ew ®a±¢Si¥š² ®S Hm eðl 15, Bl Hp M¢au¡e ew 310, Bl Hp c¡N ew 742, ¢p Hp 362, 363 ew c¡­Nl 25 na¡wn S¢jz </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">ü¡-AØfø</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">14/3/7<span style="mso-tab-count: 6;">                                                                 </span>ü¡/- B¢aL¥l lqj¡e plL¡l <span style="mso-tab-count: 2;">              </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">         </span>h¡wm¡­cn Ju¡Lg fËn¡p­Ll f­r <span style="mso-tab-count: 3;">                                    </span><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">            </span>14/3/77''</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 1.0in; text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(underlining added)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">              </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The language of the said letter in the parts underlined tends to imply that permission had already been given and details were being sought from the Mutawalli as to how the sale proceeds would be used. On the strength of this letter, the Mutawalli proceeded to sell the property in question to the respondent Nos.1-9. This aspect has been clearly explained in the order of the Administrator of Waqfs dated 04.02.82. We also note that in the said order the Administrator of Waqfs noted as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">“The matter was duly enquired upon through the local inspector as per order D/14.3.77 and the then Mutawalli Md. Sharif Chowdhury was asked to submit plan and estimate and the then Naib-Mutawalli was asked to give his comment vide this office memo No. 226-27D/14.03.77. The then Naib Mutawalli and the Mutawalli submitted a plan &amp; estimate with a separate letter by the Naib-Mutawalli Haji Nurul Islam Chowdhury according consent to the proposed transfer. Vide Dairy No.8174D/21.04.77.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">              </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The Administrator of Waqfs observed as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">“On perusal of the records it appears that the present Mutawalli Haji Nurul Islam Chowdhury although given his consent in writing to accord permission to sell 25 decimals of land as per petition of the late Mutawalli Md. Sharif Chowdhury, he i.e. the present Mutawalli Haji Nurul Islam Chowdhury by suppression and mis-representation of the facts got the Miscellaneous Case No.208/81 filed by the Administrator of Waqfs in the Court of the Sub-ordinate Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Chittagong.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">              </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">As observed by the trial Court, appellate Court and the High Court Division, the appellant did not challenge the said order of the Administrator of Waqfs, nor did he challenge the order by which the miscellaneous case was withdrawn and his application for addition of party as co-plaintiff was rejected on 18.2.82.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">              </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Property belonging to a Waqf may only be transferred by its Mutawalli after getting sanction from the Administrator of Waqfs, as provided by section 57 read with section 56 of the Waqfs Ordinance, 1962. Section 56(3) provides that any transfer made by a Mutawalli without the sanction from the Administrator of Waqfs shall be declared void, if the Administrator, within 4 months of his coming to know of such transfer, or within 3 years from the date of such transfer, whichever is later, applies to the Civil Court in this behalf. Thus, it is solely in the domain of the Administrator of Waqfs to challenge any transfer of Waqf property by a Mutawalli. It transpires that at the instigation of the plaintiff-predecessor of the appellant, the Administrator of Waqfs filed Miscellaneous Case No.208 of 1981, which was subsequently withdrawn on the direction of the Administrator of Waqfs, who in the meantime scrutinised the records and found that the Naib Mutawalli (plaintiff in the suit) had consented to the transfer.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">              </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The finding of the Administrator of Waqfs to the effect that the predecessor of the appellant-plaintiff in the suit had consented to the transfer of the property in question is a finding of fact which could have been agitated by the plaintiff in a properly constituted challenge before the concerned District Judge. But he did not do so. Hence, the finding that the transfer was valid cannot be challenged by him since there is a bar under section 102 of the Ordinance.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">              </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">In view of the above discussion, we are of the opinion that the instant appeal is devoid of merit and accordingly it is dismissed, without, however, any order as to costs.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><a href="file:///C:/Users/Hp/Downloads/masum/Issue_January_2020(1)%201/Issue__January_20(1)__C.%20A.%20598%20%20of%202009__Muhammad%20Imman%20Ali_J___AD___2.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">CIVIL<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>APPEAL<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>NO. 598 OF<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>2009</span></u></strong></a><u> </u></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(From the judgement and order dated 14<sup>th</sup> of May, 2008 passed by the High Court Division in Civil Revision No.443 of 2001)</span></p></div></div></div></div>
826	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Ashuganj Fertilizer and Chem. Co. Ltd. Vs. Md. Abu Sufian Bhu. and ors.,  (Syed Mahmud Hossain, C. J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL APPEAL NOS.96 -111 OF 2015  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Syed Mahmud Hossain, Chief Justice Hasan Foez Siddique, J And Mirza Hussain Haider, J</p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Tufailure Rahman, Senior Advocate, instructed by Mr. Md. Firoz Shah, Advocate-on-Record.,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2020(1) LNJ (AD)  </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Ashuganj Fertilizer and Chemical Company Limited, represented by its Managing Director and others:</p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Md. Abu Sufian Bhuiyan and another</p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Bangladesh Industrial Enterprises (Nationalisation) Order, 1972</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-07-13</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: justify; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: justify; Respondents.</span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(In C.A.No.111/15)</span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 4.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 14.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">Bangladesh Industrial Enterprises (Nationalisation) Order, 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">Article 11 (1)(2)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold','serif'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">Inquiries against some other officers of Bangladesh Chemical Industries Corporation indicated that the writ-petitioners were not fit for the job and as such, they should be terminated. There is nothing on record to show that during the course of inquiry held at the instance of the Ministry, the writ-petitioners were heard and they were allowed to defend their case. There is no doubt that the Government in the Ministry of Industries is the controlling authority of ZFCL but it cannot direct BCIC to remove employees of ZFCL, who were appointed by the proper authority. General direction and administration of the affairs of the business of a corporation shall vest in a Board of Directors, which may exercise all powers and do all acts and things, which may be exercised or done by the Corporation. The Board shall be subject to the superintendence and control of the Government and shall be guided, in the discharge of its functions, by such general or special instruction as may, from time to time, be given to it by the Government.</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                              </span>  (16, 18 &amp; 19)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 13.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">Bangladesh Industrial Enterprises (Nationalisation) Order, 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">Article 11 (1)(2)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">If the Ministry dictates the Corporation in all matters then the purpose of clause (1) of Article 11 will become nugatory. There is, of course, no doubt that the Ministry has the control and superintendence over the Corporation but the Ministry cannot interfere in its internal management without concurrence of the Board of Directors.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                               </span>(19)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">Secretary, EPIDC vs. Md. Serajul Haque, (1970) 22 DLR (SC)284; The Chartered Bank, Mombay, vs. The Chartered Bank Employees’ Union and another AIR 1960 (SC)919; Bangladesh Road Transport Corporation and another vs. Md. Shahidullah (2002)54 DLR (AD)124; Parjatan Corporation vs. Md. Ali Hossain and another, (2013) 65 DLR (AD)158 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt;">For the Appellants. (In all the appeals)</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt;">: </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Tufailure Rahman, Senior Advocate, instructed by Mr. Md. Firoz Shah, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">For the Respondents, In all the appeals):</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> Mr. A. Zahirul Islam, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">JUDGMENT</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><u><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps; mso-ansi-language: EN-GB;">SYED MAHMUD HOSSAIN</span></u></strong><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">All the appeals, by leave, are directed against the judgment and order dated 15.05.2014 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition Nos.1755, 1756, 1758, 1759, 1760, 1763, 1764, 1765, 1766, 1767, 1768, 1769, 1770, 1771, 1797, 1798 of 2008 making all the Rules absolute with direction.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">All the civil appeals have been heard together and are being disposed of by this common judgment as they do involve common questions of laws and facts. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The facts, leading to the filing of all the appeals, in a nutshell, are:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">All the writ-petitioners were serving in different clerical posts as Senior Clerk, MLSS, LDA-cum-Typist, Bearer, Typist, Assistant Clerk, Office Assistant etc. At the Zia Fertilizer Company Limited (hereinafter referred to as ZFCL) for several years on daily basis. The writ-petitioners applied to the ZFCL authority to appoint them permanently in the vacant posts. On consideration of their quality of service and sound performance, the authority by Memo No.ZFCL/Proshason/ LSA/7(a)/1607 dated 09.10.2006 sent a proposal to the Chief of Bangladesh Chemical Industries Corporation (BCIC), which is the controlling authority of ZFCL seeking approval under Article 13(5) of the Bangladesh Chemical Industries Enterprise (Nationalization) Order, 1972 (P. O. 27 of 1972) for the permanent appointment of the writ-petitioners against vacant posts at ZFCL. It has been further stated in the said letter that </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: TimesNewRoman; mso-bidi-font-family: TimesNewRoman;">“</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Zviv wbR wbR Kg©‡¶‡Î </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal;">E</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">−</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal;">õM</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">−</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal;">k¡NÉ </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Ae`vb ‡i‡L‡Qb| </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal;">¢L¿º </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Zv‡`i g‡a¨ AwbðqZv I nZvkv weivR Ki‡Q| Zv‡`i‡K ¯’vqxfv‡e wb‡qvM †`qv n‡j Zv‡`i Kg© ¯ú„nv e„w× cv‡e|</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">In response to the aforesaid letter dated 09.10.2006 seeking approval under Article 13(5) of the Bangladesh Chemical Industries Enterprise (Nationalization) Order, 1972 (P. O. 27 of 1972) for permanent appointment of the writ-petitioners, the Deputy Employee Chief on behalf of the Employee Chief vide Memo No. BCIC/Niog-3/ZFCL-6/45 dated 05.02.2007 intimated the Managing Director of ZFCL about the approval of BCIC for permanent appointment of the writ-petitioners at ZFCL subject to approval of the ZFCL. In the letter it was clearly stated that </span><span style="font-size: 11.5pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: TimesNewRoman; mso-bidi-font-family: TimesNewRoman;">‘‘ </span><span style="font-size: 11.5pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: TimesNewRoman; mso-bidi-font-family: TimesNewRoman;">’’</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">After getting formal approval from the Bangladesh Chemical Industries Corporation, ZFCL Authority vide Memo dated 06.02.2007 issued appointment letter to the writpetitioners and after getting the said appointment letters the writ-petitioners joined in their posts and started serving the authority to the satisfaction of all concerned. It is stated that there is no allegation from any quarter against the writ-petitioners’ service or their efficiency. Thereafter, suddenly by letter dated 29.11.2007, the Senior Assistant Secretary of the Ministry of Industries, informed the Chairman of the Bangladesh Chemical Industries Corporation that a newspaper article showed that there were certain irregularities in the appointment of 19 employees at ZFCL and that the writ-petitioners having been found unsuitable for the post, their services should be terminated. On receipt of the aforesaid Memo dated 29.11.2007, Bangladesh Chemical Industries Corporation by letter dated 05.12.2007 informed ZFCL to terminate the Service of the writ-petitioners at once. The ZFCL Authority as per direction of writ-respondent No.2, thereafter, by the impugned letter dated 11.12.2007 informed the writ-petitioners that their services were terminated and they would be entitled to one month’s pay in lieu of any prior notice.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Being aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the impugned letters dated 11.12.2007 (Annexure-B) issued by writ-respondent No.3 under the signature of writ-respondent No.5, the writ-petitioners filed the writ petitions before the High Court Division and obtained Rules Nisi in the above writ petitions.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Writ-respondent Nos.2 and 5 contested the Rules by filing affidavit-in-opposition controverting the material statements made in the writ petitions. Their case, in short, is that the writ-petitioners were appointed on purely temporary and ad-hoc basis and the same was mentioned in their appointment letters. The petitioners joined their services accepting the said terms and conditions as stated in the appointment letters and the employer had every right to terminate their services without assigning any reason and this is also the case as per provision of Bangladesh Labour Law,2006. It has been further stated that since the appointment of the writ-petitioners were irregular, they were legally terminated as per instruction made by the Ministry of Industry in terms of clause-3 of the appointment letter and that the writpetitioners cannot have any grievance against the same. It has been further stated that as per P. O. 27 of 1972, the concerned Ministry has supervisory and controlling authority over BCIC and ZFCL and as such, ZFCL is bound to carry out the instructions of the Ministry as well as Bangladesh Chemical Industries Corporation. It has been further stated that the writpetitioners’ services have been terminated in accordance with the provision of law and that the impugned orders of termination are nothing but termination simpliciter and hence the writ-petitioners cannot have any grievance against the same and that the Rules are liable to be discharged.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The learned Judges of the High Court Division, upon hearing the Rules, by the impugned judgment and order dated 15.05.2014, made the Rules absolute with direction. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Feeling aggrieved by and dissatisfied with judgment and order passed by the High Court Division, the writ-respondents as the leave-petitioners have filed Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal Nos.3028-3043 of 2014 before this Division, in which, leave was granted on 19.02.2015, resulting in Civil Appeal Nos.96-111 of 2015.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Tofailure Rahman, learned Senior Advocate, appearing on behalf of the appellants in all the civil appeals, submits that according to term and condition No.3 of the appointment letter, the writ-petitioner-respondents were terminated from service and as such, the termination in question is mere termination simpliciter and not a stigma and that the High</span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; 827	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Chattogram Dry Dock Ltd. Vs.  M.T. Fadl-E-Rabbi and others (M. Khurshid A. Sarkar, J.)</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Admiralty Suit No. 92 of 2016 </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  M. Khurshid Alam Sarkar, J</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Saifur Rashid, Advocate,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2020(1) LNJ  </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Chattogram Dry Dock Ltd</p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  M.T. Fadl-E-Rabbi (IMO No. 9078177) and others </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Evidence Act (I of 1872)</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-07-13</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;">(STATUTORY ORIGINAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 6.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 106.0pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top" width="141"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.4pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold','serif'; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">M. line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><a href="file:///C:/Users/Hp/Downloads/masum/Issue_January_2020(1)/Issue%20__January__2020(1)_Admiralty%20Suit%20No.92%20of%2016_M.%20Khurshid%20Alam%20Sarker,%20J.__3.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Petitioners</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">M.T. Fadl-E-Rabbi (IMO No. 9078177) and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Respondents</span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Evidence Act (I of 1872)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 115</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Estoppels: Its meaning and application:</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold','serif';">When a person acts on the basis of another person’s words/action/omission believing it to be true, the later is estopped from saying/doing otherwise. a person shall not be allowed to allege and prove a thing under the following circumstances; (i) when a person makes a representation (declaration/action/ omission) to another and (iii) the other has acted upon the said representation to his detriment. In other words, on the basis of a person’s representation when another person does something, subsequently the person who had made such representation shall not be allowed to deny the truth of his representation. a party is prevented by his own acts from claiming a right to the detriment of the other party who was entitled to rely on such conduct and has acted accordingly.</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                           </span>...(15, 16 and 18)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"><span style="text-decoration: none;"> </span></span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Customs Act (IV of 1969)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 18(1)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Imports and Exports (Control) Act (XXXIX of 1950)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 2(c)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Meaning of ‘Import’/‘Importation’:</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">If any good is imported into Bangladesh, duties shall be levied at a rate prescribed in the First Schedule to the Customs Act (Bangladesh Customs Tariff). This piece of Legislation does not require presentation of Bills of Entry as a precondition for levying of customs duties. All that it require is that the goods must be imported. When any goods/produce is brought into the country from a foreign country, it would be called ‘import’/‘importation’.  When any foreign thing, object, goods, which would include a foreign vessel, is brought into or comes in Bangladesh, be it without or with Bills of Entry, it is dutiable, as per the prevailing rate prescribed in the Bangladesh Customs Tariff, if the same is picked up/collected/ arrested for the purpose of home consumption, warehousing, selling to local or foreign national/country or for any other lawful purpose. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">          </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">     </span>...(25 and 29)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Words and Phrases</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Duties of Advocates<u><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></u></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">While an Advocate would be seen by this Court to be fully justified in receiving a detailed Judgment on finishing hearing of a suit or any other original substantive matter (such as Admiralty Suit, Writ Petition, Company Matter) even if the Court expresses its views dismissing the suit/discharging the Rule, however, as an officer of the Court, an Advocate is expected to assist this Court in saving its time by non-prosecuting an interlocutory application, when the same would be found by the Court without any substance after affording the opportunity of placing the arguments at length. It is to be borne in mind by the learned Advocates that since the number of Judges of this country are very negligible in comparison to the case-load, it has become very difficult for the learned Judges of this country to dispose of the substantive suit/matters and, therefore, the learned Advocates should not expect detailed Judgment on the side-issue of a suit/matter, which is already well-settled by the Apex Court of our jurisdiction. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                        </span>...(31)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Bashiruddin Ahmed Vs Secretary, Bangladesh Government, 3 BLC(AD) 179 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;
