line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></p></td><td style="width: 94.05pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md. Lutfor Rahman and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Petitioners</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Govt. of Bangladesh, represented by the Secretary, Ministry of Housing and Public Works, Bangladesh Secretariat, Ramna, Dhaka and others. </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Respondents</span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Article 102</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Unless this Division interferes, the petitioners, who for bona fide reason did not agitate grievance before the Court of Settlement, would be without forum. This Division cannot permit this to happen. Accordingly, this Division is of the view that it should exercise jurisdiction over the matter. We therefore hold that in the present circumstances, that the writ petition is maintainable. ...(19)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Abandoned Buildings (Supplementary Provisions) (Ordinance LIV of 1985)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 5(1)(a)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold','serif';">This is a mandatory precondition for inclusion of a property in the list of abandoned property under Section 5(1)(a) of the 1985 Ordinance. This is also the consistent view of both Divisions of the Supreme Court of Bangladesh,  in case of dispute, the Government must show that the possession of property has been taken by it. The onus is upon the Government because the Government has the relevant documents which would prove that it has taken possession. <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                       </span></span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">            </span>...(11 and 12)<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">     </span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Bangladesh Abandoned Property (Control Management and disposal) Order (PO 16 of 1972)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Article 7</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Abandoned Buildings (Supplementary Provisions) (Ordinance LIV of 1985)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 5(1)(a)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold','serif'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">Two legislations dealing with the same subject matter should be interpreted harmoniously. The relevant legislations are P.O. 16 of 1972 and the 1985Ordinance.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Under P.O. 16 of 1972 a property can be regarded as abandoned property subject to certain conditions. Order 7 of P.O. 16 of 1972 contains the functions of the Government in respect of abandoned properties. Under P.O. 16 of 1972, the Government is required to take possession of abandoned properites. Section 5(1)(a) of the 1985 Ordinance is attracted if and only if the Government took possession of the property. So the attributable interpretation is that Section 5(1)(a) of the 1985 Ordinance can be applied if the possession has been taken by the Government under Order 7 of P.O. 1972.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Order 18 of P.O. 16 of 1972 provides that the Government shall maintain a separate account for each abandoned property.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>P.O. 16 of 1972 also provides that Government shall impose fine on tress passers on abandoned property.</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                             </span>...(14)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Bangladesh Abandoned Property (Control Management and disposal) Order (PO 16 of 1972)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Articles 2 and 7</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Article 102</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">In respect of the property in question, the respondents failed to show that the Government took possession in accordance with the provisions of P.O. 16 of 1972. The respondents also failed to show the account for the property in question. If the predecessors of the petitioners were infact unlawfully occupying the property in question, then the Government would have proceeded against them. No such evidence was shown. To the contrary, the petitioners have annexed documents which suggest that even in 1979, the predecessor of the petitioners was the owner on record of the property in question; even in 1979 the Government received land tax from the predecessor of the petitioners. Therefore, the only logical conclusion that this Division has arrived is that the property in question is not an abandoned property and the property was erroneously included in the impugned Gazette.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                             </span>...(14)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Marzina Khatun vs Bangladesh [13 BLC (AD) 140] ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Md. Bazlur Rashid, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: right; line-height: 110%;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">For the Petitioners</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Md. Mokleshur Rahman</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: right; line-height: 110%;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">For the Respondent No. 1</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 8.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="text-decoration: none;"> </span></span></u></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 6.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="text-decoration: none;"> </span></span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Naima Haider</span></u></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">, J. <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In this application under Article 102 of the Constitution, Rule Nisi was issued in the following terms:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 7.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 27.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Let a Rule Nisi be issued calling upon the respondents to show cause as to why the inclusion 7.50 decimals of land, Housing No. 1088/1 Mouza-Ibrahimpur, J.L. No. 269, C.S. Khatian No. 11, C.S. Plot No. 268, S.A. Khatian No. 8, S.A. Plot No. 268, R.S. Khatian No. 365, R.S. Plot No. 1106, Police Station-Kafrul, Dhaka Cantonment Area, Dhaka having been enlisted in “Ka” list of Abandoned Building published in Bangladesh Gazette dated 23.069.1986 under serial No. 12, page No. 9762(4) under the provision of Abandoned Building (Supplementary Provisions) Ordinance, 1985(Ordinance LIV of 1985) should not be declared to have been made without lawful authority and is of no legal effect and as such the case prosperity in question, shall not be excluded from the said list of Abandoned Building (as contained in Annexure-J) and/or pass such other or further order or orders as to this Court may seem fit and proper.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 27.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In this writ petition, the dispute arises out of inclusion of the property/land in question, measuring 7.50 decimals, in the Bangladesh Gazette on 23.09.1986. Through this Gazette, the Government treated the property in question as abandoned property under Section 5(1) (a) of The Abandoned Buildings (Supplementary Provisions) Ordinance 1985 (“the 1985 Ordinance”).</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the instant writ petition, the petitioners claim that they are the owners of the property in question. In support, the petitioners elaborately states, with supporting documents, how the property devolved in their favour. Essentially, the petitioners acquired the property in question after the death of their father Md. Shamsul Haque. Mr. Haque became the owner of the property further to a gift from one Md. Main Uddin.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>The petitioners’ father had been in possession of the property during his lifetime. The petitioners have been in possession after their father’s death. On the land/property in question, building was constructed after obtaining permission from RAJUK. The tax for the land/property was also paid to the Government regularly till 1421 B.S. The petitioners became aware of the inclusion of the property in the Bangladesh Gazette in 1422 B.S. when the tahsilder office refused to accept the rent on the plea that the property was declared abandoned property through the Bangladesh Gazette dated 23.09.1986.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Being aggrieved by the inclusion, the petitioners moved this Division and obtained the instant Rule.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Counsel for the petitioners, taking us through the writ petition and the documents annexed, submits that the petitioners and their predecessors were in possession of the property in question and therefore, treating the property as abandoned property was illegal. He further submits that the petitioners and the predecessors paid land taxes to the Government till 1422 BS and therefore, the property cannot be treated as abandoned property. He also submits that the record of rights is in favour of the petitioners, the petitioners constructed multi storied building on the land after obtaining permission from the regulators and therefore, the land in question cannot be treated as abandoned property. On these, among other counts, the learned Counsel submits that the Rule should be made absolute with appropriate direction upon the respondents.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Rule is opposed by the respondent No.1. An Affidavit in Opposition was filed. The learned Counsel appearing for the respondent No.1, taking us through the Affidavit in Opposition submits that the property in question is abandoned property under P.O. 16 of 1972.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>The learned Counsel also submits that the writ is not maintainable as the petitioners did not agitate their grievance before alternative forum, being the Court of Settlement. The learned Counsel further submits that the instant writ petition gives rise to disputed questions of fact regarding the ownership of the property and therefore, this Division should not interfere. On these, among other counts, the learned Counsel submits that the Rule should be discharged.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">We have heard the learned Counsels at length and perused the pleadings and the documents annexed. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the event a property is treated as abandoned property, the person aggrieved is required to agitate the grievance before the Court of Settlement within a stipulated time. This is a statutory requirement. The issue is whether the petitioners ought to have or could have referred the dispute before the Court of Settlement.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 7 of the 1985 Ordinance gives opportunity to the persons claiming any right or interest in a property to apply to the Court of Settlement to exclude the particulars of the property from the list of abandoned property. However, such application is required to be filed within one hundred and eight days from the date of publication of the official Gazette. Admittedly the petitioners have not done so. The issue is whether this should bar to exercise of our supervisory jurisdiction under Article 102 of the Constitution.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Since Section 7 of the 1985 Ordinance provides an opportunity to apply to the Court of Settlement to exclude property from the list of abandoned property, the said provision also implies that the person must know of the inclusion. How else can he apply? Why else should he apply? The issue before us is whether the petitioners could be construed to have knowledge of the inclusion. We note from the documents annexed that the Government accepted land tax till 2015. Furthermore, RAJUK also issued permission for construction of multi storied building on the land in question. If the authorities treated the property as abandoned property, they would neither have accepted rent from the petitioners nor would have issued construction permit. Thus the petitioners had no reason to believe that the property in question was included in the list. By the time the petitioners realized that the property was included in the list, it became too late for the petitioners to avail the alternative remedy. The petitioners could not have agitated the grievance before the Court of Settlement. Furthermore, since the Court of Settlement had been specifically empowered by statute to exclude any property from the list of abandoned property, the petitioners could not have agitated their grievance before any other Court. This is set out in Section 6 of the 1985 Ordinance. Unless this Division interferes, the petitioners, who for bona fide reason did not agitate grievance before the Court of Settlement, would be without forum. This Division cannot permit this to happen. Accordingly, this Division is of the view that it should exercise jurisdiction over the matter. We therefore hold that in the present circumstances, that the writ petition is maintainable.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The property in question was listed in the Bangladesh Gazette under Section 5(1)(a) of the 1985 Ordinance. This is set out in the impugned notification (Annexure-J). Section 5(1)(a) of the 1985 Ordinance is set out below for ease of reference:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 45.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“ 5(1) The Government shall, after the commencement of this Ordinance and before the 31<sup>st</sup> day of December, 1988, publish, from time to time in the official gazette-</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 45.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">list of buildings the<u> possession of which have been taken as abandoned property, under the President’s Order</u>;</span></em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> (emphasis added)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .25in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It is clear from the wordings of Section 5(1)(a) of the 1985 Ordinance that the Government must take possession of the property in question; this is a mandatory precondition for inclusion of a property in the list of abandoned property under Section 5(1)(a) of the 1985 Ordinance. This is also the consistent view of both Divisions of the Supreme Court of Bangladesh. The Hon’ble Appellate Division, in the case of <u>Marzina Khatun vs Bangladesh [13 BLC (AD) 140] </u>took the view that in certain circumstances, actual possession is not necessary; constructive possession would suffice. The issue before this Division is whether the Government took possession of the property in question, either actual or constructive.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">This Division is of the view that in case of dispute, the Government must show that the possession of property has been taken by it. The onus is upon the Government because the Government has the relevant documents which would prove that it has taken possession. In the instant case, we note that land tax had been paid by the predecessor of the petitioners prior to inclusion of the property in the Bangladesh Gazette. This prima facie show that the Government did not take possession of the property in question. Had it been otherwise, the Government would not have accepted land tax from the predecessors of the petitioners. Furthermore, we also note that the Government accepted tax on the property till 2015. We also note that RAJUK issued permission for construction of multistoried building over the property in question. Therefore, there is a presumption of possession in favour of the petitioners and their predecessors. Now, the issue is whether the respondent No.1 provided any documents to controvert the presumption of possession in favour of the petitioners. In the Affidavit in Opposition, the respondent No.1 did not annex any document(s) which show that the Government took possession of the property in question. The respondent No.1 did not even make such assertion. We are therefore, inclined to hold that the petitioner has prima facie satisfied this Division of the continued possession of the property in question.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Counsel for the respondent No.1 submits that the property in question is abandoned property within the meaning of P.O. 16 of 1972 and therefore, the property had been correctly included in the impugned Gazette.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The settled position of law is that two legislations dealing with the same subject matter should be interpreted harmoniously. The relevant legislations are P.O. 16 of 1972 and the 1985Ordinance.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Under P.O. 16 of 1972 a property can be regarded as abandoned property subject to certain conditions. Order 7 of P.O. 16 of 1972 contains the functions of the Government in respect of abandoned properties. Under P.O. 16 of 1972, the Government is required to take possession of abandoned properites. Section 5(1)(a) of the 1985 Ordinance is attracted if and only if the Government took possession of the property. So the attributable interpretation is that Section 5(1)(a) of the 1985 Ordinance can be applied if the possession has been taken by the Government under Order 7 of P.O. 1972.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Order 18 of P.O. 16 of 1972 provides that the Government shall maintain a separate account for each abandoned property.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>P.O. 16 of 1972 also provides that Government shall impose fine on tress passers on abandoned property. In respect of the property in question, the respondents failed to show that the Government took possession in accordance with the provisions of P.O. 16 of 1972. The respondents also failed to show the account for the property in question. If the predecessors of the petitioners were infact unlawfully occupying the property in question, then the Government would have proceeded against them. No such evidence was shown. To the contrary, the petitioners have annexed documents which suggest that even in 1979, the predecessor of the petitioners was the owner on record of the property in question; even in 1979 the Government received land tax from the predecessor of the petitioners. Therefore, the only logical conclusion that this Division has arrived is that the property in question is not an abandoned property and the property was erroneously included in the impugned Gazette.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Counsel further submits that there are disputed questions of facts. Accordingly, intervention is uncalled for. This argument is misconceived. The issue before this Division is whether the inclusion of the property in question in the impugned Gazette Notification was in accordance with law. As stated above, for the inclusion to be in accordance with law, the Government must take possession. The respondent No.1 despite having all the documents relating to this property, failed to produce a single document which shows that the Government took possession of the property in question, either actual or constructive. To the contrary, the petitioners have shown evidence of possession,</span><span style="font-size: 11pt;">pre 1986 as well as post 1986. Therefore, we are not entirely sure how a disputed issue arose in the given facts and circumstances.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">16.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In light of the above, we are inclined to hold that the inclusion of the property in question in the impugned Gazette Notification was illegal and without lawful authority. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">17.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">This Division therefore, disposes the Rule. This Division holds that the property in question was wrongly treated as abandoned property through Bangladesh Gazette dated 23.09.1986. All executives, who are not impleaded in the instant writ petition, are directed not to treat the property in question as abandoned property. <u>The writ respondents are directed to formally release the property in question</u> (particulars are set out in Bangladesh Gazette dated 23.09.1986 in page 9764(2) under serial No. 12) from Bangladesh Gazette dated 23.09.1986 within 1 (one) month from the date of receipt of our Judgment and order without fail. (emphasis added)</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">18.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">With the aforesaid observation and directions, the Rule is disposed of without any order as to costs.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">19.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Communicate our Judgment and Order at once for immediate compliance.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///C:/Users/Hp/Downloads/masum/Issue_January_2020(1)/Issue%20__January__2020(1)__W.P%20_13133%20of%2015_Naima%20Haider,%20J.__2.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">WRIT </span></u></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">PETITION NO. 13133 OF 2015</span></u></strong></p></div></div></div></div>
829	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Md. Rafiqul Islam Chowdhury Vs.  Md. Abul Kalam Azad and aor,   A.K.M. Shahidul Huq, J.)</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Civil Revision No. 1984 of 2014 </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  A.K.M. Shahidul Huq, J</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Rowshan Alam Khan, Advocate,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2020(1) LNJ  </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Md. Rafiqul Islam Chowdhury</p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Md. Abul Kalam Azad and another</p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-07-13</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;">(CIVIL REVISIONAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 6.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 106.0pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top" width="141"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.4pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold','serif'; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">A.K.M. Shahidul Huq, J</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">09.01.2019</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 15.6pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="21"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><a href="file:///C:/Users/Hp/Downloads/masum/Issue_January_2020(1)/Issue%20__January__2020(1)_Civil%20Rivision.%20No.1984%20of%202014_A.K.M%20Shahidul%20huq,%20J.__5.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></p></td><td style="width: 94.05pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md. Rafiqul Islam Chowdhury</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Petitioner</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md. Abul Kalam Azad and another</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">opposite parties</span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> </span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Section 115(1)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold','serif';">Since both the Courts below concurrently decreed the suit in favor of the opposite parties under section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure there is very little scope to interfere with the concurrent findings of facts which are immune from attack under the revisional jurisdiction. As such I am constrained not to interfere with the concurrent findings of the Courts below. Consequently the instant Civil Revision filed under section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure is devoid of any substance.</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; letter-spacing: -.3pt;"> <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">           </span>...(46)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Md.Habibullah vs. Mr. Sher Ali Khan and others 11 ADC 405, Shambhu Nath Poddar vs. Bangladesh Railway and others 43 DLR (AD) 82, Abdur Gafur and others vs.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Md. Abdur Razzak and others 62 DLR (AD) 242, Sakina Khatoon and others vs. Ibrahim Ahmed Khan and others 2 MLR (AD) 330, Additional Deputy Commissioer (Revenue), Jhalakathi vs. Syed Nuruzzaman and others 6 MLR (AD) 116, Mahmud Ali and another vs. Bangladesh and others 1986 BLD (AD) 56, Md. Shah Alam vs. Mosammat Farida Begum 17 BLD (AD) 145, Chairman, Mongla Port Authority vs. Kazi Brothers and others 59 DLR (AD) 9 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Rowshan Alam Khan, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: right; line-height: 110%;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. A.K. M. Shamsuddin, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: right; line-height: 110%;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">For the opposite parties</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="text-decoration: none;"> </span></span></u></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="text-decoration: none;"> </span></span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">A.K.M. Shahidul Huq, J. </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">This Rule was issued calling upon the opposite parties to show cause as to why the impugned judgment and decree dated 09.3.2014 (decree signed on 16.3.2014) passed by the learned Special District Judge, Dinajpur in Other Class Appeal No. 134 of 2009 disallowing the appeal and thereby<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>affirming the judgment and decree dated 23.7.2009 passed by the learned Assistant Judge, Nowabgonj, Dinajpur in Other Class Suit No. 95 of 2004 decreeing the suit should not be set-aside and/or pass such other or further order or orders as to this Court may seem fit and proper.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The short facts for disposal of the instant Rule is that the plaintiff filed an Other Class Suit No. 95 of 2004 in the Court of Assistant Judge, Nawabpur, Dinajpur against the petitioner for declaration of title over the suit land contending inter alia that the defendant No. 1 purchased the suit land and was in possession. In need of money the defendant offered to sell the suit land. the plaintiff agreed to purchase the suit land and the consideration money was fixed at Tk. 94,000/- and an unregistered bainapatra was executed on 18.07.1997 in the presence of the witnesses and the defendant No. 1 received Tk. 50,000/- cash and promised to execute and register a sale deed whence he will get the rest Tk. 44,000/- from the plaintiff. The plaintiff was an illiterate and stupid and the defendant No. 1 was a B.Sc Teacher. The plaintiff gave the rest Tk. 44,000/- to the defendant No. 1 on 02.12.1997 and went to the scribe Shahajahan Ali of sub-registrar officer who is nephew of the defendant No. 1 and had his well known scribe written the suit sale deed and took Tk. 12,000/- as stamp fee cost from the plaintiff and then he informed him that the stamp was not available and for that the parties should go to the sub-registrar<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>office after some days. The plaintiff asked the scribe to return<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>his money but the defendant No. 1 assured him that the scribe was his nephew and nothing to worry. On 31.12.1997 the parties to the suit went to the sub-registrar office and registered the sale deed but the same was not read over to the plaintiff. The next day the defendant No. 1 delivered the possession of the suit land to the plaintiff. The plaintiff got the original deed on 01.01.2002 and the witness, Khaleque told<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>him that the suit deed not contained the entire suit land, it contained 2.26 acres of land out of 5.63 acres. Which make the plaintiff astonished. On 17.03.2002 the plaintiff along with the witnesses went to the house of the defendant No. 1 and asked him about the matter and asked him to return the rest of the money but the defendant No. 1 refused to return and for that the plaintiff filed a criminal case being No. 317C of 2002 under section 406/420 of the Penal Code. In that case the defendant No. 1 promised to return the money before bail but after enlarged on bail he refused to return the money. On 17.04.2004 the Court to framed charge against the defendant No. 1 under section 420/406 of the Penal code and that time he promised to register the suit land if the plaintiff withdrawn the criminal case. Finally on 15.07.2004 the plaintiff along with the witnesses went to the defendant No. 1 to register the suit land but the defendant No. 1 also refused to do so and hence the suit of the plaintiff. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The defendant No. 1 contested the suit by filing written statement, denying all the material allegation of the plaint and contending inter alia that the suit of the plaintiff is not maintainable by law as because the plaintiff filed the suit for declaration of title instead of Specific Performance of contract and as such the suit is liable to be dismissed. The defendant No. 1 purchased 6.23 acres of land through 7(seven) different deeds and while owning and possessing of his purchased land, proposed to sell 1.70 acre of land the plaintiff agreed to purchase the same that later the plaintiff purchased<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the proposed land by registered sale deed. Subsequently the defendant No 1 in<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>need of money sold 2.26 acres of land by a registered sale deed No. 7663 dated 31.12.1997 in favour of the plaintiff. The defendant No. 1 also executed a baina deed by a registered deed being No. 5062 dated 22.07.1999 to the plaintiff. The plaintiff breach the terms and condition of contract and for that the defendant No. 1 did not register the land to<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the plaintiff. The plaintiff after purchasing 3.96 acres of land from the defendant No. 1 trying to acquire other property by filing criminal case being No. 78C of 2002 under section 420/406 of the Penal code which was dismissed and after that the plaintiff also filed another criminal Case No. 371C of 2002 in which charge was framed against the defendant No. 1 and against that order the defendant No.1 filed a criminal Revision No. 147 of 2004 which is now pending in the learned Additional Sessions Judge, Court No. 3, Pabna. The defendant No. 1 never transferred the possession of 5.63 acres of land to the plaintiff. 1.67 acres of land out of 3.96 acres is in possession through adhiar and the suit of the plaintiff.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">After conclusion of the trial the learned Assistant Judge, Nawabganj Upazilla, Dinajpur was pleased to decree the suit in favour of the plaintiff by its judgment and decree dated 23.07.2009 (decree signed on 30.07.2009).</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Being aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the judgment and decree passed by the learned Assistant Judge, Nawabganj, Dinajpur the defendant petitioner as appellant institute an appeal before the learned District Judge, Dinajpur which was registered as Other class Appeal No. 134 of 2009 and on transferred it was heard by the learned Special District Judge, Dinajpur and after hearing was pleased to disallow the appeal and thereby<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>affirming the judgment and decree dated 23.07.2009 and 30.07.2009 by the Assistant Judge court, Nawabganj, Dinajpur in Other Class Suit No. 95 of 2004 by its judgment and decree dated 09.03.2014 (decree signed on 16.03.2014).</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Rowshan Alam Khan the learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the petitioner submits that an unregistered bainanama has been executed on 2<sup>nd</sup> Sraban 1404 and on that day plaintiff paid Tk. 50,000/- (fifty thousand) only to the defendant out of Tk. 94,000/- (ninety four thousand) only for purchasing 5.56 acres of land<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>and the rest would be paid by the plaintiff to the defendant within 5<sup>th</sup> Agrahayan 1404 B.S. i.e. the plaintiff would pray the rest amount of tk. 44,000/- (forty four thousand) only within 4 months and 3 days but the plaintiff misdirected the court by mentioning the tenure to pay the rest amount of Tk. 44,000/-(Forty four thousand) only within five months in his examination-in-chief and he stated that </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal;">“flha£Ñ 5 j¡­pl j­dÉ hœ²£ 44,000/- V¡L¡ 1ew ¢hh¡c£ hl¡hl fÐc¡e L¢l­m ®p S¢j ®l¢S¢øÌ L­l ¢c­h”</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>which is completely contrary with the unregistered bainanama. Here it is also mentioned that the plaintiff failed to pay the rest money to the defendant within stipulated time stated in the bainanama for this reason a meeting was held in Mirzapur Primary School’s filed where the plaintiff along with<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>other persons were present and in their presence the unregistered bainapatra was revoked and 2.26 acres of land was sold by the defendant to the plaintiff through registered deed on 31.12.1997 but both the courts below misreading and misunderstanding the real facts and circumstances of the case passed the impugned judgment and decree and committed an error of law as well as on facts in the decision occasioning failure of justice.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He further submits that according to the amicable settlement between the plaintiff and defendant the plaintiffs did not pay the rest amount of Tk. 44,000/- (Forty four thousand) only to the defendant and a deed has been executed and registered on 03.12.1997 in connection with 2.26 acres of land but both the courts below misdirected themselves and passed the impugned judgment and decree and thereby committed an error of law and facts in the decision occasioning failure of justice.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He next submits that both the courts below did not apply their judicial mind in drawing up the judgment and decree which led to erroneous decision of both the courts below. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He next submits that both the courts below did not properly examine the evidence on record in its true perspective which led to miscarriage of justice.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He next submits that both the courts below committed an error of law resulting in an error in the decision occasioning failure of justice in not believing the defendant’s case although the defendant proved his case by adducing proper witnesses.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He next submits that the suit is barred by limitation and the plaintiff failed to file this suit within 6(six) years from the date of knowledge but both the courts below did not consider this legal aspect at the time of passing the impugned judgment and decree and thereby committed an error of law as well as on facts in the decision occasioning failure of justice.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He also submits that both the courts below committed an error of law resulting in an error in the decision occasioning failure of justice in not believing the defendants case although there is no contrary being proved by the plaintiff and in the absence of any legal pleadings having been made by the plaintiffs there was no case on the side of the plaintiff before the court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He further submits that the suit of the plaintiff is a simple declaration of title but both the courts below misdirected themselves pronouncing the judgment and decree as like as specific performance of contract and thereby committed an error of law as well as on facts in the decision occasioning failure of justice.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Rowshan Alam Khan, the learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the petitioner lastly submits that neither of the Court below did consider the rejection of the amendment application in its true perspective and on due and proper consideration of the averments as made in the plaint and most illegally and arbitrarily passed the impugned judgment which was based on total non-consideration of the averments as made in the plaint vide order dated 18.02.2009.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The rule is being contested by the opposite parties by filing counter affidavit. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. A.K.M Shamsuddin, the learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the opposite parties submits that in paragraph No. 7-11 of the Rule petition are misconceived and the same not be sustained in law and the learned Courts below rightly and correctly passed the impugned judgment and decree and as such the Rule is liable to be discharged. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the opposite parties also submits that the Court of appeal below, after considering the facts and circumstances of the case and the evidence on records, both oral and documentary, very rightly and correctly passed the impugned judgment and decree and as such this Hon’ble court has nothing to interfere under its revisional jurisdiction and as such the Rule is liable to be discharged. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the opposite parties further submits that both the Courts below, after considering the facts and circumstances of the case and the evidence on records and having found title and exclusive possession of the plaintiffs in the suit land decreed the suit and as such this Hon’ble court has nothing to interfere under it’s revisional jurisdiction and as such the Rule is liable to be discharged. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the opposite parties argued that the appellate Court below being the last court of fact, very rightly and correctly passed the impugned judgment and order and there is no question of law involved in this revisional application and the appellate Court below did not commit any error in law resulting an error in his decision and as such the Rule is liable to be discharged. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the opposite parties has also argued that this revisional application is misconceived and as such the instant rule is liable to be discharged for the ends of justice.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the opposite parties has further argued that the petitioner has got no cogent ground and legal reason in this revision and as such the petitioners cannot get any relief from this court under its revisional jurisdiction. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;
