mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the opposite parties has submitted that the grounds taken in the rule petition all based on facts and no points of law are involved in this revisional application and as such the rule is liable to be discharged. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the opposite parties also submits that the grounds taken in the Rule petition all vague, indefinite, false and baseless and as such the rule is liable to be discharged.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the opposite parties has argued that both the lower appellate and trial court on elaborate perusal of evidences both oral and documentary have concurrently found the claim of the plaintiff opposite party No. 1 as just and correct and on the other hand the claim of the defendant petitioner to be false and baseless and thereby decreed the suit and as such the revisional application bear no good ground to be interfered with and the rule issued in the instant revisional application is liable to be discharged.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the opposite parties has submitted in a same breath the ground taken by the defendant petitioner are not cogent and good ground and as such those are not sustainable in law. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; Habibullah Vs. Mr. Sher Ali Khan and others reported in 11 ADC page-405.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate also referred the case of Shambhu Nath Poddar -Vs. Bangladesh Railway and others reported in 43 DLR (AD) page 82.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">28.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the opposite parties has further referred the case of Abdul Gafur and others Vs. Md. Abdur Razzak and others reported in 62 DLR (AD) page 242.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">29.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate also referred the case of Sakina Khatoon and others Vs. Ibrahim Ahmed Khan and others reported in 2 MLR (AD) page 330.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">30.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the opposite parties also referred the case of Additional Deputy Commissioner (Revenue), Jhalakathi Vs. Syed Nuruzzaman and others reported in 6 MLR (AD) page 116.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">31.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the opposite parties further referred the case of Mahmud Ali and another Vs. Bangladesh and others reported in 1986 BLD (AD) page-56.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">32.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He also referred the case of Md. Shah Alam Vs. Mosammat Farida Begum reported in 17 BLD (AD) page 145.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">33.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the opposite parties lastly referred the case of Chairman, Mongla Port Authority Vs. Kazi Brothers and others reported in 59 DLR (AD) page-09.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">I have perused the impugned judgment and decree of the last court of fact considered the submissions as advanced by the learned Advocate appearing for the petitioner as well as the learned Advocate for the opposite parties on due and proper consideration of documents on record and the citations referred and on due consideration of the submissions as advanced by the learned Advocate for the petitioner as well as the learned Advocate for the opposite parties. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">35.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Before arriving at a proper finding it is utmost important to go through the citations as referred by the learned Advocate for the opposite parties in the case of Md. Habibullah Vs. Mr. Sher Ali Khan and others reported in 11 ADC where our Apex court held that;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .75in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“Since the Court of fact on detail discussion of the evidence on record held that the plaintiffs failed to prove their exclusive possession in respect of the land in suit and that the last Court of fact also held that the land in respect whereof decree for<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>permanent injunction has been sought is unspecified and as the said finding did not suffer from any mis-reading or non-consideration of the evidence or in other words any legal evidence was not left out in making the decision in the case by the Court of fact the High Court Division was in serious error in reversing the concurrent finding of fact of the courts below……..”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">36.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of Shambhu Nath Poddar -Vs. Bangladesh Railway and others reported in 43 DLR (AD) 82 where our Apex court held that;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .75in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“A revisional Court acts beyond its jurisdiction in setting aside concurrent finding of fact, when there is no misreading and misappreciation of the evidence on record.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">37.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Now I go through the next citation as referred by the learned Advocate in course of his submissions is the case of Abdul Gafur and others Vs. Md. Abdur Razzak and others reported in 62 DLR (AD) 242 where our Apex court held that;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .75in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“Courts below also concurrently found that the defendants have failed to prove their right title, interest and possession in the suit lands by adducing oral and documentary evidence. These findings of fact are not immune from interference by the High Court Division in exercise of revisional jurisdiction in the absence of misreading or non-consideration of the evidence on record. The learned Judge of the High Court Division has exceeded its jurisdiction in interfering with the concurrent findings of fact, which is liable to be interfered with.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">38.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Now I go through the next citation as referred by the learned Advocate in course of his submissions is the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>case of Sakina Khatoon and others Vs. Ibrahim Ahmed Khan and others reported in 2 MLR (AD) where our Apex court held that;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .75in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“The finding of fact arrived at by the trial Court as well as the appellate Court on proper appreciation of the evidence on record cannot be interfered with under section 115 of the Code of Civil Procedure by the High Court Division.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .75in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">39.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Now I go through the next citation as referred by the learned Advocate in course of his submissions is the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>case of Additional Deputy Commissioner (Revenue), Jhalakathi Vs. Syed Nuruzzaman and others reported in 6 MLR (AD) where our Apex court held that;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .75in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“Unless there is a case of non-consideration or misreading of any material evidence on record resulting in an error in the decision occasioning failure of justice concurrent finding of fact cannot be interfered with”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">40.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Now I go through the next citation as referred by the learned Advocate in course of his submissions is the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>case of Mahmud Ali and another Vs. Bangladesh and others reported in 1986 BLD (AD) where our Apex court held that;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .75in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“Whether appellate Court is to find out the points for determination and give its judgment in an appeal if the absence of any defect in the judgment of the trial Court pointed out by the appellant-When, the appellate Court does not differ with the findings and conclusions of the trial Court it should express its concurrence with them” It is not the duty of the appellate Court when it<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>agrees with<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the views of the trial Court to restate the effect of evidence or to reiterate the reasons given by the trial court-Expression of general agreement with reasons given by the Court decision of which is under appeal would ordinarily suffice.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">41.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Now I go through the next citation as referred by the learned Advocate in course of his submissions is the case of Md. Shah Alam Vs. Mosammat Farida Begum reported in 17 BLD (AD) where our Apex court held that;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .75in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“Without reversing the findings of facts concurrently arrived at by the Courts below on the grounds covered by section 115 C.P.C. the High Court Division has no jurisdiction to disturb the findings of facts. It cannot superimpose itself as a third Court for fresh appreciation of the evidence on record this being not the function of a Court of revision.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">42.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Now I go through the next citation as referred by the learned Advocate in course of his submissions is the case of Chairman, Mongla Port Authority Vs. Kazi Brothers and others reported in 59 DLR (AD) where our Apex court held that;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .75in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“When the appellate Court agrees with the views of the trial Court it is not required to restate the effect of evidence or to reiterate the reasons given by the trial Court and expression of general agreement with reasons given by the Court, decision of which is under appeal would ordinarily suffice.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">43.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">I find since both the Courts below on due and proper consideration of both oral and documentary evidences concurrently passed the decree in favour of the plaintiff as such the same is immune from attack under the revisional jurisdiction of this Hon’ble Court. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">44.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The submissions as advanced by the learned Advocate for the petitioner I do not find any merit in the Rule. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">45.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On the contrary, the submissions as advanced by the learned Advocate for the opposite parties I find merit and the citation as referred by the learned Advocate for the opposite parties in support of his contention are fully applicable in the facts and circumstances of the present case.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">46.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">I find that since both the Courts below concurrently decreed the suit in favour of the opposite parties under section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>there is very little scope to interfere with the concurrent findings of facts which are immune from attack under the revisional jurisdiction. As such I am constraint to interfere with the concurrent findings of the Courts below. Consequently the instant Civil Revision filed under section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure is devoid of any substance.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">47.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In result, the Rule is discharged without any order as to cost.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">48.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The impugned judgment and decree dated 09.03.2014 and 16.03.2014 passed by the learned Special District Judge, Dinajpur in Other Class Appeal No. 134 of 2009 disallowing the Appeal and thereby affirming the judgment and decree dated 23.07.2009 decree signed on 30.07.2009 passed by the learned Assistant Judge, Nawabgonj, Dinajpur in Other Class Suit No. 95 of 2004 decreeing the suit is hereby affirmed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">49.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The order of stay granted earlier at the time issuance of the Rule is hereby recalled and vacated.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">50.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The office is hereby directed to transmit a copy of this judgment to the concerned Court forthwith for information and necessary action.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///C:/Users/Hp/Downloads/masum/Issue_January_2020(1)/Issue%20__January__2020(1)_Civil%20Rivision.%20No.1984%20of%202014_A.K.M%20Shahidul%20huq,%20J.__5.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">Civil Revision No. 1984 of 2014</span></u></strong></a></p></div></div></div></div>
830	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Md. Shahid Ullah  Vs.  Jubilee Bank Limited and others, (M. Khurshid A. Sarkar, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> COMPANY MATTER NO. 315 OF 2017 </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Muhammad Khurshid Alam Sarkar, J</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Md. Kamrul Alam (Kamal), Advocate,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2020(1) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2020</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Md. Shahid Ullah</p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Jubilee Bank Limited and others </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Companies Act (XVIII of 1994)</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-07-13</p><!DOCTYPE html><div class="WordSection1"><h2 align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><!-- [if gte vml 1]><v:shapetype id="_x0000_t202" coordsize="21600,21600" o:spt="202" path="m,l,21600r21600,l21600,xe"> <v:stroke joinstyle="miter"/> <v:path gradientshapeok="t" o:connecttype="rect"/></v:shapetype><v:shape id="_x0000_s1026" type="#_x0000_t202" style='position:absolute; left:0;text-align:left;margin-left:-12pt;margin-top:-36pt;width:456pt; height:36pt;z-index:251657728' stroked="f"/><![endif]--><!-- [if !vml]--></h2><span style="font-family: arial black, sans-serif;"><span style="font-size: 20px;">The Lawyers &amp; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 14.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 15.0pt;">2020(1)</span></strong></h2><h2 align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-align: center;">Report of the Decisions of the <strong style="font-size: 13pt;">High Court Division</strong><span style="font-size: 13pt;"> of the Supreme Court of </span>Bangladesh<span style="font-size: 13pt;">.</span></h2></div><p style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 13.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-language: AR-SA;"> </span></p><p><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p> </p><p><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(STATUTORY ORIGINAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><p> </p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 106.0pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top" width="141"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold','serif'; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Muhammad Khurshid Alam Sarkar</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold','serif'; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">, J</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> </strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">04.02.2020</span></strong></td><td style="width: 15.6pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="21"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span> <a href="file:///C:/Users/Hp/Downloads/masum/Issue_January_2020(1)/Issue%20__January__2020(1)__Com.%20Ma.%20No.315%20of%2017_M.%20Khurshid%20Alam%20Sarker,%20J.__1.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></td><td style="width: 94.05pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="125"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md. Shahid Ullah</span> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">. . .Petitioner</span></em></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Jubilee Bank Limited and others </span> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">. . .</span></em></strong><u> </u><strong><em><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Respondents</span></u></em></strong> <strong><em><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;"><span style="text-decoration: none;"> </span></span></u></em></strong> <strong><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> </span></em></strong></td></tr></tbody></table><p> </p><p><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Companies Act (XVIII of <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">1994)</span></span></strong></p><p> </p><p><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 85 (3)<u></u></span></strong></p><p> </p><p><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Under Section 85(3) of the Companies Act, though the AGM of any company can be ordered <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">suomotu</em> by this Court to be called, held and conducted without even receiving an application from any person, however, if an application is filed by any person claiming himself to be a shareholder, it is incumbent upon the said person to satisfy this Court that s/he is a genuine shareholder of the company whose AGM/other meeting could not be held for some unavoidable reason. </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">              </span>...(1)</span></strong></p><p> </p><p><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"><span style="text-decoration: none;"> </span></span></u></strong></p><p> </p><p><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Duty of the State-functionaries and citizen of this country towards the Father of Nation:</span></u></strong></p><p> </p><p><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Let it be known by all the State-functionaries, the Government/non-Government authorities and citizen of Bangladesh, and also by the people across the globe, that Bangabandhu Sheikh Mujibur Rahman is recognized as the Father of the Nation of Bangladesh by the supreme law of Bangladesh i.e. the Constitution of Bangladesh and, therefore, all of us are constitutionally duty bound to pay homage to the Father of the Nation. And, when the duty is about apprehending the killers of the Father of the Nation and confiscating their assets and properties, it becomes more onerous for the State-functionaries and the Government authorities to perform their respective duties more earnestly and mindfully. On this august eve of the birth centenary of the Father of the Nation, it is expected that the concerned Government authorities and the State-functionaries shall <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">suomotu</em> take necessary steps to annihilate the physical and moral strength of the killers of the Father of the Nation towards paying off the debt this nation owes to Him.</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>...(5 and14)</span></strong></p><p> </p><p><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Md. Kamrul Alam (Kamal), Advocate</span></p><p> </p><p><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p> </p><p><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">Mr. A.K.M. Badrudduza, Advocate</span></p><p> </p><p><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the Respondent No. 2-RJSC</span></em></strong></p><p> </p><p><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Muniruzzaman, Advocate</span></strong></p><p> </p><p><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the Respondent No. 3-Bangladesh Bank</span></em></strong></p><p> </p><p><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p> </p><p><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">M. Khurshid Alam Sarkar</span></u></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">, J. </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">By adopting crooked legal devices, some unscrupulous persons have been claiming themselves as the shareholder-directors of the respondent No. 1-company, namely, Jubilee Bank Limited (hereinafter referred to either as the JBL or as the Bank or as the company), whose only office at Jainpur Bazar, Khoksha, Kushtia is being run for decades by its employees, but without having any director or shareholder. Out of the aforesaid unscrupulous persons, the present petitioner Mr. Shahid Ullah has filed the instant case being the Company Matter No. 315 of 2017 under Section 81(2) read with Section 85(3) of the Companies Act, 1994 (shortly, the Companies Act) for calling, holding and conducting the AGM of the JBL and succeeded to obtain Order on 07.12.2017 from this Court for calling, holding and conducting the AGMs of the JBL. Although the petitioner is claiming himself to be the shareholder-director of the JBL, but he did not explain to this Court as to how he became a shareholder of the JBL. In the backdrop of the fact that there is no existence of the original Memorandum of Association (MoA) and Articles of Association (AoA) of the JBL, neither in the office of the Registrar of Joint Stock Companies and Firms, nor in the Bangladesh Bank and even not in the office of the JBL, it was the mandatory duty of this Court either to find out the real shareholders of the JBL towards effective adjudication upon this case or to dismiss this case. Under Section 85(3) of the Companies Act, though the AGM of any company can be ordered <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">suomotu</em> by this Court to be called, held and conducted without even receiving an application from any person, however, if an application is filed by any person claiming himself to be a shareholder, it is incumbent upon the said person to satisfy this Court that s/he is a genuine shareholder of the company whose AGM/other meeting could not be held for some unavoidable reason.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The other case being the Company Matter No. 61 of 2012 was filed previously, in the year 2012, before this Court by one Mr. M.B.I. Munshi claiming himself to be the Chairman of the JBL, under Section 81(2) read with 85(3) of the Companies Act for calling, holding and conducting the AGMs of the JBL and the Court had permitted the aforesaid so called shareholder Mr. Munshi to call, hold and conduct the AGMs of the JBL along with some directions. It appears to this Court that at the time of allowing the aforesaid application under Section 81(2) read with 85(3) of the Companies Act, the Hon’ble presiding Judge of this Court was not made acquainted about the standing of Mr. Munshi as to how he claims himself to be the shareholder-director as well as the Chairman of the JBL. In the backdrop of the facts that there was no existence of the original Memorandum of Association (MoA) and Articles of Association (AoA) of the Jubilee Bank Limited, neither in the office of the Registrar of Joint Stock Companies and Firms (RJSC), nor in the Bangladesh Bank and even not in the office of the JBL, the claim of Mr. MBI Munshi that he possesses a notarized copy of the MoA and AoA, ought to have been rejected outright by this Court.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The petitioners in both the cases i.e. in the Company Matter No. 61 of 2012 and in the instant Company Matter No. 315 of 2017 have attempted to persuade this Court by simply stating that the original MoA and AoA have been lost and due to non-availability of the above instruments, the petitioners managed to obtain some photocopies of the MoA and AoA and, upon getting the same authenticated by the Notary Public, those were submitted to the office of the Registrar of Joint Stock Companies and Firms.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Faced with the above scenario, this Court vide its Orders dated 23.06.2019 and 16.07.2019 made some enquires to the RJSC (respondent No.2) as well as to the Bangladesh Bank (respondent No.3) and, in reply thereto, both the offices informed that they do not have any original copy of the MoA and AoA or any original documents of the JBL, such as Schedule-X, Form-XII etc, in their custody. Further, upon an enquiry it was confirmed by the employees and officers of the registered office of the JBL situated at Jainpur Bazar, Khoksha, Kushtia (which is the only office of the JBL) that they also do not have any original copy of the MoA, AoA, Members’ Register Book (which is commonly known as Shares Register) or any other documents, such as Schedule-X, Form XII etc. On top of that, they do not know who are the Chairman, Managing Director, directors and shareholders of this company. Resultantly, no Return was ever filed by any of the officials from the office of the JBL or nor did the RJSC ever receive any valid Return from any other person. Therefore, this Court is of the view that it was the legal duty of the RJSC to delete the name of this company from its Record/Register invoking Section 346 of the Companies Act. </span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On the other hand, admittedly the Jubilee Bank Limited was established by Major (dismissed) Md. Abdur Rashid and his cohorts, who are the self-declared killers of the Father of the Nation, Bangabondhu Sheikh Mujibur Rahman. And, since Major (dismissed) Md. Abdur Rashid, after being convicted with death sentence, remains absconding and the Court has ordered to confiscate all his assets and properties, the State is under a legal obligation to ensure that all his assets and properties have been confiscated. By virtue of the Court’s Order of the confiscation of the assets and properties of the killers of Bangabondhu, the Bangladesh Bank, in collaboration with the Ministry of Home Affairs and the Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs, could have taken necessary legal steps to confiscate the killers’ shares and, thereafter, could have approached this Court for winding up of the JBL. Let it be known by all the State-functionaries, the Government/non-Government authorities and citizen of Bangladesh, and also by the people across the globe, that Bangabandhu Sheikh Mujibur Rahman is recognized as the Father of the Nation of Bangladesh by the supreme law of Bangladesh i.e. the Constitution of Bangladesh and, therefore, all of us are constitutionally duty bound to pay homage to the Father of the Nation. And, when the duty is about apprehending the killers of the Father of the Nation and confiscating their assets and properties, it becomes more onerous for the State-functionaries and the Government authorities to perform their respective duties more earnestly and mindfully. </span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Furthermore, the killers of the Father of the Nation obtained the banking license of the JBL from the Bangladesh Bank on 25.06.1984 subject to the following conditions;</span></p><p> </p><p><a name="_GoBack"></a><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">1.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The company will raise its paid-up capital to Tk. 5 lacs within December, 1984.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The company shall confirm its loan operation to gold loan only for the present.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The company shall not make any loan or advances on the security of its own shares or grant unsecured loans or advances to any of its directors or to firm or private companies in which it or any of its directors is interested as partner or managing agent or to any individuals, firms or privates companies in shares where any of the directors is a guarantor. The company shall not make loans or advances to any of its directors or to individuals, firms or companies in which it or any of its directors is interested as partner, director, managing agent or guarantor, as the case may be, without the approval of the majority of the directors of the company, excluding the director concerned.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The company shall strictly follow instructions given by Bangladesh Bank from time to time relating to interest or deposits and advances.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The company shall maintain a sum equivalent to at least two percent of its time liabilities and five percent of its demand liabilities in Bangladesh in cash as cash reserve with itself or in the current account opened with Bangladesh bank or its agent or partly in cash with itself and partly in such account or accounts.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The company shall submit to Bangladesh Bank before the 15<sup>th</sup> day of every month a return showing reserve hold by it on Thursday of each week of the preceding month with particulars of its equivalent time liabilities in Bangladesh as cash each Thursday or if Thursday is a closed holiday, at the close of business or the preceeding working day.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The company shall maintain in cash, gold or unsecured approved securities valued at a price not exceeding the current market price an amount which shall not at the close of business on any day be less than twenty five percent of its total time an uni demand liabilities in Bangladesh, The company shall furnish to Bangladesh bank a monthly return relating to maintenance of liquid assets and its time uni demand liabilities in Bangladesh<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>at the close of business on each Thursday during the month or if Thursday is a public holiday, at the close of business on the preceeding working day.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The company shall maintain at the close of business on any day assets in Bangladesh value of which shall not be less than 80% of its time uni demand liabilities in Bangladesh. A monthly return in prescribed form and manner showing particulars of company’s assets and its total demand and time liabilities in Bangladesh at the close of business in every Thursday shall be furnished to Bangladesh Bank before the close of the month authorizing that to which the return reflects.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The accounts and balance sheet of the company together with auditor’s report as passed in the Annual General Meeting shall be published in the prescribed manner and three copies thereof shall be furnished as return to the Bangladesh Bank within three months of the close of the period to which they relate.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">  </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">All other provisions of Banking Companies Ordinance 1962 which are generally applicable to the banking companies will also be applicable to the company unless specific exemption is given.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">  </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The license or a certified copy thereof shall be kept displayed at the place of business in respect of which it has been granted.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">  </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The location of the place of business as indicated in the license shall not be changed except with the prior approval of the Bangladesh Bank. </span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">After issuance of the above-mentioned license, it was the statutory duty of the Bangladesh Bank to monitor and oversee the functions and performances of this Bank. However, from the affidavit filed by the Bangladesh Bank, it appears to this Court that from the date of issuance of the license on 26.06.1984, the Bangladesh Bank has never issued any notice seeking explanation from the JBL as to why it is not filing any periodical and monthly report to the Bangladesh Bank. Moreover, after enactment of the Banking Companies Act, 1991 (hereinafter referred to as the Banking Companies Act), the JBL was statutorily obligated to take license from the Bangladesh Bank under Section 31 of the Banking Companies Act, but till date the Bangladesh Bank did not issue any notice to the JBL informing it that in the eye of law there is no existence of this Bank for not obtaining license under Section 31 of the Banking Companies Act. Moreover, the JBL has also never complied with the condition of keeping the minimum reserve capital as required by Section 13 of the Banking Companies Act. </span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">While the Bangladesh Bank is empowered by the provisions of Banking Companies Act not only to seek explanations from the JBL but also empowered to close down the activities of this Bank, this Court takes judicial notice of the Bangladesh Bank’s stance, as it transpires from the averments and statements made by the officials of Bangladesh Bank, that they are still confused as to their authority over a Bank which was created by a mere letter issued by the Bangladesh Bank itself. When this Court asked the Bangladesh Bank to submit the original MoA and AoA of the JBL before this Court, it was informed that Bangladesh Bank do not have any type of papers/documents of the JBL. Whenever any incorporated company wishes to obtain a license from the Bangladesh Bank for carrying out banking business, usually an application is filed by the said company together with its MoA and AoA, but for some unknown reason or for the reason best known to the authority of the Bangladesh Bank, no such paper (MoA or AoA) of the JBL has been retained by the Bangladesh Bank. More interestingly, usually the Registrar of Joint Stock Companies and Firms (RJSC) issues a certificate of incorporation only after receiving the MoA and AoA of a company, but in the case of JBL, the RJSC also did not bother to keep a copy of MoA and the AoA of the JBL. Previously, when the Bangladesh Bank was asked to carry out an investigation about the activities of the JBL, it was revealed that there is only one office of the JBL which has been carrying on its business at Jainpur Bazar, Khoksha, Kustia, and the officers and employees of the JBL working in the said office had informed the Bangladesh Bank authority that neither they have any Share Register Book nor do they have any MoA and AoA of the JBL. This Court, thus, finds it to be a bizarre situation inasmuch as an incorporate body can never be allowed by the concerned authority to be in existence without having any Share Register Book and its MoA and AoA. Some bogus shareholders of the JBL apparently cooked up a story that they possess the xeroxed copies of the MoA and AoA of the JBL and, after making the same notarized, the same have been submitted to the RJSC. It is not fathomable to this Court as to how the Registrar of Joint Stock Companies and Firms (RJSC) received the aforesaid photocopied MoA and AoA from some pseudo shareholders of the JBL.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Even if these unscrupulous petitioners seek to produce any share certificate to the RJSC, the RJSC should not believe their contentions given the fact that if there is no Share Register of the company, it is difficult for anyone to identify himself or herself, as the case may be, as the shareholder of a company merely on the basis of holding a share certificate.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">    </span></span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">With the above observation, this Court is of the view that an explanation from the Governor of Bangladesh Bank is required as to why the Bangladesh Bank is not taking appropriate and necessary action against the JBL to wrap up its activities, since the JBL has never complied with the conditions/stipulations as embodied in the license dated 25.06.1984 and why the Bangladesh Bank is not coming up with an application for winding up of the JBL.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Under these circumstances, this Court finds it appropriate to pass the following Orders and Directions upon the RJSC as well as upon the Bangladesh Bank;</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">i.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">              </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Registrar of Joint Stock Companies and Firms (RJSC) is directed to strike off the name of the Jubilee Bank Ltd from its Record/Register upon complying with the relevant provisions of Section 346 of the Companies Act.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">ii.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Governor of Bangladesh Bank is directed to inform this Court as to who were the responsible officials (i.e. Governor/s, Deputy Governor/s, Executive Director/s, Director/s, General Manager/s, Deputy General Manager/s and other officers) for monitoring the activities of this company, from the date of issuance of its license dated 25.06.1984 till date and, whether they have ever been asked by the Governor or any other high-ranking official to show cause as to their failure to carry out their respective legal duties.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">iii.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Why the Bangladesh Bank did not come up with an application for winding up of this banking company.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">              </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">After completion of the required formalities under Section 346 of the Companies Act, the Registrar of Joint Stock Companies and Firms is directed to file an affidavit-in-compliance within 1(one) week thereafter.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">              </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">And, the Governor of the Bangladesh Bank is hereby directed to file an affidavit-in-compliance within 05.03.2020.</span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">              </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Office is directed to communicate this Order at once to the (i) Governor of Bangladesh Bank and (ii) the Registrar of Joint Stock Companies. On this august eve of the birth centenary of the Father of the Nation, it is expected that the concerned Government authorities and the State-functionaries shall <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">suomotu</em> take necessary steps to annihilate the physical and moral strength of the killers of the Father of the Nation towards paying off the debt this nation owes to Him. </span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Office is further directed to serve a copy of this Order (i) to the Hon’ble Prime Minster, (ii) the Hon’ble Law Minister, (iii) the Hon’ble Home Minister, (iv) the Hon’ble Finance Minister and (v) the Hon’ble Commerce Minister for their perusal and necessary actions. </span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Additionally, Mr. A.K.M. Badrudduza (who is the learned Advocate for the RJSC) and Mr. Muniruzzaman (who is the learned Advocate for the Bangladesh Bank) are directed to take this Order by hand from the Bench Officer of this Court and communicate the same to their respective parties, so as to assist this Court towards expeditious disposal of the matter. </span></p><p> </p><p><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">              </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Let the matter be posted in the daily cause list on 05.03.2020 under the column ‘For Compliances’. </span></p><p> </p><p><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></strong></p><p> </p><p><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed.</span></strong></p><p> </p><p><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p> </p><p><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p> </p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><a href="file:///C:/Users/Hp/Downloads/masum/Issue_January_2020(1)/Issue%20__January__2020(1)__Com.%20Ma.%20No.315%20of%2017_M.%20Khurshid%20Alam%20Sarker,%20J.__1.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">CO</span></u></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">MPANY MATTER NO. 315 OF 2017</span></u></strong></div></div><p> </p></div></div>
831	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Oram Limited Vs.  Reckitt Benckiser (Bangladesh) Limited    (Borhanuddin, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Arbitration Appeal No. 03 OF 2014 </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Borhanuddin, J. And Sardar Md. Rashed Jahangir, J.</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. M. Moyeen A. Firozee with Mr. Muhammad Rafiul Islam and Mr. Md. Muazzem Hossain, Advocates,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2020(1) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Oram Limited</p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Reckitt Benckiser (Bangladesh) Limited</p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Arbitration Act (I of 2001) Section 55(1)</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-07-13</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;">(STATUTORY ORIGINAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 106.0pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top" width="141"><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold','serif'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Borhanuddin</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">, J.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.45pt .0001pt 35.1pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">And</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Sardar Md. Rashed Jahangir, J.</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">27.10.2019</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 15.6pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="21"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><a href="file:///C:/Users/Hp/Downloads/masum/Issue_January_2020(1)/Issue%20__January__2020(1)_Arbitration%20case%20No.3%20of%2014_Borhanuddin,%20J.__8.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></p></td><td style="width: 94.05pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Oram Limited</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Appellant</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Reckitt Benckiser (Bangladesh) Limited</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Condemned-Convict</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> </span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Arbitration Act (I of 2001)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Section 55(1)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Any claim made beyond the period of limitation prescribed by the Limitation Act will be barred by limitation and the arbitral tribunal will have to reject such claim as barred by limitation.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">            </span>...(25)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Arbitration Act (I of 2001)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;
