In all such cases it may be left upon to courts to lift the veil to enquire whether the scheme is aimed at achieving the above objective and is a genuine attempt at validating irregular appointments. In a democratic set up like ours, which is governed by rule of law, the supremacy of law is to be acknowledged and absence or arbitrariness has been consistently described as essence of rule of law. The unquestionable authority is always subject to the authority of the Constitution.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">It is important to cite the case of Secretary to Government, School Gobinda Swamy and others [(2014)] 4SCC 769. In that case Supreme Court of India considering the case of State of Rajasthan and others V. Daya Lal and others reported in AIR 2011 SC 1193 has made observation about the scope of regularization of irregular or part-time appointments in all possible eventualities and laid down well-settled principles relating to regularization relevant in the context of the issues involved therein. The same is as under:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .75in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">“The High Courts, in exercising power under Article 226 of the Constitution will not issue directions for regularisation, absorption or permanent continuance, unless the employees claiming regularisation had been appointed in pursuance of a regular recruitment in accordance with relevant rules in an open competitive process, against sanctioned vacant posts. The equality clause contained in Articles 14 and 16 should be scrupulously followed and Courts should not issue a direction for regularisation of services of an employee which would be violative of the constitutional scheme. While something that is irregular for want of compliance with one of the elements in the process of selection which does not go to the root of the process, can be regularised, back door entries, appointments contrary to the constitutional scheme and/or appointment of ineligible candidates cannot be regularised. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .75in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(ii) Mere continuation of service by a temporary or ad hoc or daily-wage employee, under cover of some interim orders of the court, would not confer upon him any right to be absorbed into service, as such service would be ?litigious employment?. Even temporary, ad hoc or daily-wage service for a long number of years, let alone service for one or two years, will not entitle such employee to claim regularisation, if he is not working against a sanctioned post. Sympathy and sentiment cannot be grounds for passing any order of regularisation in the absence of a legal right.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The submission of Mr. Dolon so far the same relates to doctrine of legitimate expectation is concerned the doctrine can be invoked if the decisions of the administrative authority affect the person by depriving him of some benefit or advantage which either (i) he had in the past been permitted by the decision-maker to enjoy and which he can legitimately expect to be permitted to continue to do until there have been communicated to him some rational grounds for withdrawing it on which he has been given an opportunity to comment; or (ii) he has received assurance from the decision- maker that they will not be withdrawn without giving him first an opportunity of advancing reasons for contending that they should not be withdrawn. (See Lord Diplock in Council for Civil Services Union v. Minister of Civil Service 1985 AC 374). </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">There is no case that any assurance was given by the Government or the department concerned while making the appointment in development project or on daily wages that the status conferred on him will not be withdrawn until some rational reason comes into existence for withdrawing it. The very engagement was against the constitutional scheme. Though, there is a case that the Government had made regularisations in the past of similarly situated employees, the fact remains that in some cases such regularisations were done pursuant to judicial directions. Moreover, the invocation of the doctrine of legitimate expectation cannot enable the employees to claim that they must be made permanent or they must be regularised in the service though they had not been selected in terms of the rules for appointment. The fact that in certain cases the court had directed regularisation of the employees involved in those cases cannot be made use of to found a claim based on legitimate expectation. The argument if accepted would also run counter to the constitutional mandate. The argument in that behalf has therefore to be rejected. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">When a person enters a temporary employment in the development project or gets engagement as a contractual or casual worker and the engagement is not based on a proper selection as recognised by the relevant rules or procedure, he is aware of the consequences of the appointment being temporary, casual or contractual in nature. Such a person cannot invoke the theory of legitimate expectation for being confirmed in the post when an appointment to the post could be made only by following a proper procedure for selection and in cases concerned, in consultation with the Public Service Commission. Therefore, the theory of legitimate expectation cannot be successfully advanced by temporary, contractual or casual employees. It cannot also be held that the Government has held out any promise while engaging these persons either to continue them where they are or to make them permanent. The Government cannot constitutionally make such a promise. It is also obvious that the theory cannot be invoked to seek a positive relief of being made permanent in the post.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Employment in a development project or casual employment is meant to serve the exigencies of administration. In our judgment in C.A. No.460 of 2017 we have said that continuance of service for long period in the development projects or contractual or temporary basis confer no right to seek regularisation in service. The person who is engaged on temporary or in project is well aware of the nature of his employment and he consciously accepted the same. They are not entitled to seek regularisation as they are not working against any sanctioned posts. It is our consistent view that unless the appointment is in terms of the relevant rules/regulations and after a proper competition among qualified persons, the same would not confer any right on the appointee.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">28.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">If it is a contractual appointment, the appointment comes to an end at the end of the contract, if it were an engagement or appointment on daily wages or casual basis, the same would come to an end when it is discontinued. Similarly, a temporary employee could not claim to be made permanent on the expiry of his term of appointment. It has also to be clarified that merely because a temporary employee or a casual wage worker is continued for a time beyond the term of his appointment, he would not be entitled to be absorbed in regular service or made permanent, merely on the strength of such continuance, if the original appointment was not made by following a due process of selection as envisaged by the relevant rules. It is not open to the court to prevent regular recruitment at the instance of temporary employees whose period of employment has come to an end. The courts must be careful in ensuring that they do not interfere unduly with the economic arrangement of its affairs by the State or its instrumentalities or lend themselves the instruments to facilitate the bypassing of the constitutional and statutory mandates.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">29.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">While directing to regularise the service in the revenue budget of the persons who have been serving in the project or on contract basis or “no work no pay” basis, the Court ought to have taken into consideration whether their appointments were made in consonance with the constitutional scheme and statutory rules or not. If disregard of the rules and by-passing of the Public Service Commission are permitted, it will open a backdoor for illegal recruitment without limit. If the person who accepts an engagement either in the development project or on contract basis or casual in nature he accepts the employment with open eyes. It may be true that they are not in a position to bargain at arm's length since they might have been searching for some employment so as to eke out their livelihood and accepts whatever they get. But on that ground alone, it would not be appropriate to jettison the constitutional scheme of appointment and to take the view that a person who has got employment in the Project or on contract basis or casual basis should be directed to be absorbed in revenue budget. By doing so, it will be creating another mode of public appointment which is not permissible. The result of such appointments would be to keep recruitment rules and Public Service Commission in cold storage.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">30.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The Constitution is the supreme law of the State. All the institutions be it legislature, executive or judiciary, being created under the Constitution, cannot ignore it. The dictum - “Be you ever so high, the law is above you” is applicable to all, irrespective of his status, religion, caste, creed, sex or culture. Henry D Bracton - “The King is under no man but under the God and the Law”. No one is above the law. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">31.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">It is to be noted that the Government has no authority to issue any orders granting regularization/ absorption or appointment in violation of the Constitutional scheme and recruitment rules in force. All recruitment in matters of Public employment must be made in accordance with prevailing rules. While dealing with the concept of recruitment the Supreme Court of India has categorically laid down that the expression “recruitment” would mean recruitment in accordance with the Rules and not <strong><em>dehors </em></strong>the same and if an appointment is made <strong><em>dehors </em></strong>the Rules, it is not appointment in the eye of law. (ref: R.S. Garg V. State of UP (2006) 6SCC 430 and University of Rajasthan V. Prem Lata-AIR 2013 SC 1265). Similarly, the High Court Division in exercising power under article 102 of the Constitution will not issue any direction for transfer/absorption/ regularization or permanent continuance, unless employees claiming so had been appointed in pursuance of regular recruitment in accordance with relevant rules in open competitive process, against sanction posts. The BRDB, an autonomous body, while making any recruitment must strictly follow its rules and no appointment can be made in the BRDB in contravention of its rules which is not a conformity with article 29 of the Constitution. Similarly, all the statutory bodies/Corporations/ autonomous organizations must strictly follow their respective service Rules while making any recruitment in any permanent post.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">32.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">It is true that in their heydays of life the respondents are serving on exploitative terms with no guarantee of livelihood to be continued and in old age they are going to be made destitute, there being no provision for pension, retirement benefits etc. The employment cannot be on exploitative terms.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">33.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">When the employees of the development projects or casual employees appointed as stop-gap arrangement have put in for considerable years of service in the posts and their works have been approved but they could not be regularized, the only provision provides for them is to qualify the requisite examination and in such circumstances, they would get relaxation of upper age limit. If they are not selected, at the end of the day, they would return home from their respective working place with empty hand. It is the duty of the Government/employers to provide some benefits to them, on the basis of the period of service they rendered, so that they may not fall in extreme hardship otherwise the families of the those employees would face economic ruination.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">34.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">However, sympathy, empathy or sentiment by itself, cannot be a ground for passing an order where the litigants miserably fail to establish legal right. It is true that the respondents had been working for a long time, the same by itself would not be a ground for directing regularization of the service.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">35.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">In view of the discussion made above, this Court is of the view that the writ petitioners are not entitled for any relief as sought for.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">36.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">With the observations made above, all the civil petitions are disposed of. Judgments and orders impugned are hereby set aside.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><a href="file:///C:/Users/Hp/Downloads/masum/Issue_January_2020(1)%201/Issue__January_20(1)__C.%20A.%20994,%20990,%20993%20%20of%202018__Hasan%20Foez%20Siddique_J___AD___3.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><em><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">CIVIL PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL NOS.994 OF 2018</span></u></em></strong></a><strong><em><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"> WITH 990 AND 993 OF 2018.</span></u></em></strong><u> </u></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 8.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 9.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(From the judgment and order dated 14.03.2017 and 22.03.2017 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition Nos7741, 8925 and 14780 of 2016.)</span></p></div></div></div></div>
834	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">The State Vs.  Md. Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique    (Soumendra Sarker, J.)</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Death Reference No.78 of 2014  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Soumendra Sarker, J    And Shahed Nuruddin, J</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Md. Aminul Islam, D.A.G with Ms. Shamsun-nahar (Laizu) and Ms. Farhana Afroze, A.A.Gs,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2020(1) LNJ </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  The State </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Md. Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique (absconding) </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Penal Code (XLV of 1860)</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-07-13</p><!DOCTYPE html><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></p></td><td style="width: 94.05pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The State</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Petitioner</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Md. Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique (absconding)</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Condemned-Convict</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> </span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Penal Code (XLV of 1860)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 300</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">The condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique with the previous intention to murder the victim Atiqur Rahman Atique which was pre-meditative, under the ambit of section 300 of the Penal Code committed the murder.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                               </span>...(48)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Evidence Act (I of 1872)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 8</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">The absconding condemned-convict and his accomplices the appellant Sumon @ Mama Sumon and Khokon are directly involved in the occurrence of killing the victim Atique and under section 8 of the Evidence Act, 1872 the abscondence of the condemned-convict and Sumon after misusing the bail privilege being on guilty conscience, is a strong corroboration to the prosecution case that they are the culprits. The extra-judicial confession which is transpires from the testimony of the witnesses, are also a corroboration of the prosecution case as well as the confession made by the confessing condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">      </span>...(49)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898) </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 164 and 364</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">On meticulous consideration of the evidences on record along with the case record and scanning the material exhibits including the medical examination report, FIR, inquest report and the confessional statement of the condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique, it transpires that the series of evidences as adduced from the side of the prosecution, has corroborated one another as to the link of this case and the learned Magistrate who recorded the confessional statement of the principal accused the condemned-convict Shafique, during recording of the statement strictly complied with the provisions laid down in section 164 and 364 of the Code of Criminal Procedure and it was clearly explained to the accused before recording of his confessional statement that, (i) the learned Magistrate is not an officer of police but a Magistrate; (ii) that he is not bound to make a confession; (iii) that if does make a confession it may be used in evidence against him; (iv) that he should not say anything because others have told him to say it but is at liberty to say whatever he really desires to say; (v) that he should say nothing which is untrue.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                      </span>...(43)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">ABM Nazmus Sakib Ashik –vs.- State</span></em></strong><strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">, 12 BLC (AD) 203;<span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> Abul Hossain –vs.- State</span>, 46 DLR 77; <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Nausher Ali Sarder –Vs.- The State</span>, 39 DLR (AD) 194 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                                      </span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Md. Aminul Islam, D.A.G with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Ms. Shamsun-nahar (Laizu) and</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Ms. Farhana Afroze, A.A.Gs</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: right; line-height: 110%;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">For the State</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mrs. Hasna Begum, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">For the State Defence</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">No one appears</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">For the appellant</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="text-decoration: none;"> </span></span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Soumendra Sarker, J. </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">This reference under section 374 of the Code of Criminal Procedure has been made by the learned Metropolitan Sessions Judge, Sylhet for confirmation of the sentence of death passed on the condemned-convict namely Md. Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique (absconding) in Sessions Case No.1808 of 2013 (previous Sessions Case No.736 of 2012) arising out of Kotwali Model Police Station Case No.88, dated 30.11.2010 corresponding to G.R. Case No.1164 of 2010 under section 302/34 of the Penal Code.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The co-accused of this case Sumon @ Mama Sumon against whom the learned Sessions Judge awarded lifelong imprisonment with a fine of Tk.10,000/- (Ten thousand) in default to pay the fine, additional imprisonment for a term of two months under the above mentioned sections of the Penal Code, has filed a criminal appeal being No.3378 of 2015.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The Death Reference and the aforesaid Appeal have been heard together and are being disposed of by this single judgment.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The prosecution case as made out in the ejahar in a nutshell can be stated thus: One Haji Md. Khorshed Ali, son of late Md. Abdul Motaleb of village 12/A, Kumarpara, Ward No.18, Kotwali police station under Sylhet District lodged the First Information Report (FIR) with Kotwali Model Police Station before the Officer-in-Charge on 30.11.2010contending <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">inter alia</em> that the informant is the proprietor of Hotel Anurag situated at Dhupa dighir Uttarpar of Sylhet town and he was an immigrant of United Kingdom. Due to his old age with different diseases he returned back to this country and as a proprietor of the above mentioned Hotel started the same. The further case of the informant is such that his son the victim of this case, Atiqur Rahman @ Atique used to reside in London and prior to three years of the occurrence, the informant asked him to come back and the deceased Atiqur Rahman @ Atique after his return to this country was entrusted to supervise and manage the Hotel ‘Anurag’. The deceased Atiqur Rahman @ Atique got him introduced with the condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman Shafiq through one Mosharaff, a businessman of Latif Centre, Sylhet. The condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman was a businessman of VCD and DVD and he used to sale the same to the deceased Atiqur Rahman and that the condemned-convict Shafique used to come to the deceased very often and stayed in his hotel as a boarder. On 23.11.2010 the convict Shafiqur Rahman hired the room No.322 of that hotel, identifying him as a son of one Hajee Rahmat Ullah and Shahebjadi Begum and he stayed there untill the date of occurrence i.e. up to 29.11.2010. On the date of occurrence at about 3.00 p.m. at the request of the convict Shafiqur Rahman the deceased Atiqur Rahman @ Atique returned back to the hotel Anurag and went to the room No.322. After some time of his arrival in the said place of occurrence room, the convict Shafiqur Rahman and his two accomplices while where leaving the hotel, the Managers of that Hotel namely Salauddin and Shahabuddin asked the convict Shafiqur Rahman and his two accomplices as to where they are going. In reply to that, they told to the Managers that, for collecting money from S.A. Paribahan they are going outside. Subsequently, the General Manager of the hotel namely Mahmuduzzaman Jewel finding the mobile phone of the deceased Atiqur Rahman stopped, along with 4/5 employees of that hotel started to look after Atiqur Rahman, who was their junior boss and at a stage of searching, they went in front of room No.322 and hearing sound of water falling inside the said room No.322 which was under lock and key, with the help of duplicate key of the room opened the room and found the deceased Atiqur Rahman @ Atique fastened by a rope in his legs, hands, neck and waist and the mouth of the deceased Atique at that time was closed by a scotch tape. Finding that condition of the deceased Atique, the General Manager told the driver of the deceased namely Alamgir to bring the informant Hajee Md. Khorshed Ali from his residence. The General Manager informed the Rapid Action Battalion (RAB) and police requesting them to come to the place of occurrence. Subsequently, the informant along with his wife and the deceased’s wife coming to the hotel found the victim Atiqur Rahman @ Atique in the aforesaid condition and became senseless. After some time, the members of RAB and police force coming to the place of occurrence found the deceased and the police seized a Tiger Energy drink bottle from the place of occurrence room having some poisonous substance therein. They also seized some CD and VCD which were scattered inside the room. The mobile phone set and money bag of the deceased were missing, but the wristwatch of the deceased was on the floor of that room. The further case of the informant is such that the body of his son Atique was sent to Sylhet Osmani Medical College Hospital, from where he was declared ‘dead’. Subsequently, the condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique made a mobile phone call from his mobile phone No. ‘0175206307’ to other mobile phone of the deceased Atique at 01.20 a.m. being No. ‘01746065732’ and that phone call was received by the paternal father-in-law of the deceased namely Badrul Islam. The convict Shafiqur Rahman by that phone call wanted to know the condition of Atique, disclosing his identity as a friend of Atique. The phone number which was used by the condemned-convict Sofique was known to the hotel boy Mizan, inasmuch as in that phone number prior to the occurrence Sofique requested the hotel boy Mizan on different occasions to give flexi load from outside of the hotel.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Subsequently, after getting First Information Report, investigation was started by the concerned Kotwali Police Station, Sylhet and one Sub-Inspector Md. Khasrul Alam Badal and Sub-inspector Md. Abdul Alim were entrusted to investigate the case. During investigation the condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman Shafique was arrested and he confessed his guilt in killing the deceased Atikur Rahman @ Atik before a Magistrate, 1<sup>st</sup> Class and his confessional statement was recorded by the learned Magistrate under section 164 of the Code of Criminal Procedure.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>After closer of the investigation, the investigating officer finding prima-facie ingredients of the commission of offence against the convicted accused, namely Shafiqur Rahman Shafique and his accomplices Sumon @ Mama Sumon and Khokon, submitted charge sheet No.445 dated 18.06.2011 under section 302/34 of the Penal Code.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">While the case was ready for trial, it was sent to the learned Metropolitan Sessions Judge, Sylhet. The learned Metropolitan Sessions Judge after framing charge on 11.09.2012 under section 302/34 of the Penal Code read over and explained the same to the presentee accused persons Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique and Sumon @ Mama Sumon, who pleaded not guilty and claimed to be tried. The other convicted person Khokon having been absconded, the charge was not possible to read over and explain to him.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">During trial one State Defence lawyer was appointed to defend the absconding accused persons.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The prosecution at the time of trial has examined as many as 17 witnesses including the informant Hajee Md. Khorshed and the learned Magistrate, who recorded the confessional statement of the convict Shafiqur Rahmain @ Shafique.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">After the close of evidence from the side of the prosecution since only the condemned-convict Shafique was present in the accused-dock and the other two accused were absconding, he was examined under section 342 of the Code of Criminal Procedure and at that time the condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique pleading him not guilty declined to adduce evidence and claimed to be tried.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">From the trend of cross-examination of the witnesses and examination of the condemned-convict Shafique under section 342 of the Code of Criminal Procedure the case of the defence is such that the accused are innocent and in no way connected with the killing of the deceased Atiqur Rahman @ Atique.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">After trial of the sessions case the learned Metropolitan Sessions Judge, Sylhet considering the evidence and materials on record as well as facts and circumstances of the case, finding the convict persons guilty, sentenced them under section 302/34 of the Penal Code. The condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique was sentenced to death and his other co-accused Sumon @ Mama Sumon and Khokon (all along absconding) was sentenced to suffer imprisonment for life with fine of Tk.10,000/- (Ten thousand) each, in default to payment of fine, to suffer additional imprisonment of two months each.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Out of the said judgment and order of conviction and sentence this Death Reference No.78 of 2014 has been sent for the condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman and for the other convicted person Sumon @ Mama Sumon Criminal Appeal No.3378 of 2015 was preferred against the judgment and order of conviction and sentence against him.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">With regard to the Death Reference as well as Criminal Appeal No. 3378 of 2015 Mr. Md. Aminul Islam, the learned Deputy Attorney General with Ms. Shamsun-nahar (Laizu) and Ms. Farhana Afroze, the learned Assistant Attorney Generals appeared on behalf of the State. While Mrs. Hasna Begum was appointed state defence lawyer for the absconding accused. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Md. Aminul Islam, the learned Deputy Attorney General (hereinafter DAG) submits that the FIR of the case was lodged on 30.11.2010 at 22.10 hours andthe date of occurrence was 29.11.2010 and the time of occurrence was between 3.04 p.m. to 3.30 p.m. The place of occurrence was Hotel Anurag, 2<sup>nd</sup> Floor, Room No.322. The learned DAG further submits that after proper investigation of the case police submitted charge sheet under section 302/34 of the Penal Code on 18.06.2011. The charge was framed by the learned Metropolitan Sessions Judge, on 11.09.2012 and out of 31 charge-sheeted witnesses, 17 witnesses were examined by the prosecution, those who have successfully proved the case of the prosecution beyond all reasonable doubt. There is an extra-judicial confession, in this case and about this confession, the prosecution witness No.2, 11, 12 and 13 testified before the Court. The learned DAG also submits that the principal accused of this case is the condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique, who has confessed his guilt under section 164 of the Code of Criminal Procedure and clearly implicated the other co-accused of this case as of his two accomplices in the occurrence of killing the victim Atiqur Rahman @ Atique. The learned DAG argued that the Managers of the hotel Anurag, the prosecution witness No.3 and 7 categorically in their testimony testified that they have seen the convict persons and the prosecution case was totally corroborated by the witnesses including the managers. The learned DAG submits that the investigating officers of the case had no necessity to produce any witness to identify the assailants through T.I. parade, since there is a clear(distinct) video footage of the accused persons which was in the close circuit camera of the Hotel Anurag and that video footage was seized by the investigating officer and preserved, from where it is apparent that the two accomplice of the principal accused Shafique were accompanied by Shafique at the time of occurrence. The learned DAG submits that, without any mental or physical torture, fear or threat after the apprehension the condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique, when he(Shafique) wanted to confess his guilt, he was produced before the learned Magistrate, 1<sup>st</sup> Class and the learned Magistrate complying the provisions of law properly, recorded the confessional statement of the condemned-convict Shafique under section 164 of the Code of Criminal Procedure and it is from the confessional statement itself that for reflection, three hours time was given to the convict Shafique before his 164 statement and as such there is nothing to discard the confessional statement of the condemned-convict Shafique. The learned DAG lastly submits that the prosecution witness No.2 Alamgir, who is the driver of the deceased as well as the informant, is a very important witness of this case, who is competent enough to corroborate the prosecution case. The Assistant Manager of Hotel Anurag the witness No.3 is also an important witness and the witness No.2, 3 7 and 10 are the direct ocular witnesses, who has witnessed the convicted persons to leave the place of occurrence immediately after the occurrence. The witness No.11 of the prosecution is also an important witness, who has talked with the condemned-convict over telephone after the occurrence. The witness No.12 and 13 are the witnesses of extra-judicial confession and the inquest report of the deceased which was immediately after the occurrence at 16.45 hours of the date of occurrence and has clearly corroborated the injuries which were found in the dead body of the deceased Atique. From the contents of this report it is crystal clear that there is no subsequent embellishment and the FIR is very much consistent with the inquest report and postmortem report of the deceased, wherefrom it is clear that there was a distinct mark of strangulation and that the link of the occurrence has been well proved from the evidences on record and it is also well proved that it was a preplanned cool-blooded murder, since the rope which was used in tiding in the neck of the victim was brought by the assailant Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique prior to the occurrence from outside. The learned DAG in support of his contention has referred a decision of this Court reported in 55 DLR 116 and relying upon the said decision in his concluding submission submits that the prosecution has successfully discharged their onus of proof<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>by sufficient competent tangible and credible evidence and it is also proved that prior to the confession of the principal accused Shafique before the learned Magistrate, (P.W.16, Mr. Shahabuddin Masum) there was no torture, threat or provocation to him by anybody including the police and therefore, the judgment and order of conviction and sentence passed by the learned Metropolitan Sessions Judge, Sylhet should be upheld.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">As against the aforesaid argument, Mrs. Hasna Begum, the learned Advocate appearing as State Defence lawyer in support of the defence submits that, against the condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique in the instant case there is no eye witness in support of the prosecution case and there is no T.I. parade by which the assailants of the occurrence were identified. The learned State Defence Advocate further submits that there is no pre-meditation of the condemned-convict Shafique prior to the occurrence and there are several contradictions among the witnesses, who were examined in support of the prosecution case. The learned State Defence counsel lastly submits that the confessional statement of the condemned-convict Shafique is not true and voluntary and it was not properly recorded by the learned Magistrate and the driver of the informant namely Alamgir, who was examined as prosecution witness No.2 admittedly has no appointment letter and as such the evidence of the driver cannot be relied on and there is no paper relating to business relationship of the deceased with the condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique and as such the Death Reference is liable to be rejected.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">In respect of the Criminal Appeal filed on behalf of the convict-appellant Sumon @ Mama Sumon, none appeared to make any submission at the time of hearing despite; the matter has been posted in the daily cause list of this bench for days together with name of the learned Advocate for the appellant. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">In view of the argument advanced from both the sides, let us now scan the evidence adduced from the side of the prosecution and cross-examination of the prosecution witnesses including other evidence of this case. In the instant case, prosecution have examined as many as 17 witnesses including the Doctor, who did the postmortem of the dead body and the learned Magistrate, who recorded the confessional statement of the condemned-convict Shafique under section 164 of the Code of Criminal Procedure.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">P.W.1 of the prosecution is the informant of this case Hajee Md. Khorshed Ali. This witness in his testimony testifies that he is the informant of this case and proprietor of the place of occurrence Hotel Anurag. This witness also testifies that the victim Atiqur Rahman @ Atique happens to be his son and he was killed brutally. This witness in support of his ejahar corroborated the same in his deposition and at a stage categorically testified that after the occurrence the accused Shafique and his two accomplices while were leaving the hotel, the hotel Manager Salahuddin and Shahabuddin finding the accused asked them, as to where they are going and in reply, the accused Shafique told that they are going to S.A. Paribahan for bringing money. The informant of this case in his testimony identified his signature in the ejahar and clearly testifies that the ejahar was written and typed according to his statement and going through the ejahar he put his signature therein. He has identified the ejahar and his signature therein which has been marked as Exhibit-‘1’ and ‘1/1’ respectively. The informant in his deposition also testified that the accused Shafique was arrested by the members of Rapid Action Battalion (RAB) on 15.02.2011 from Dhaka, who confessed his guilt after that, before a Judicial Magistrate under section 164 of the Code of Criminal Procedure. The informant has identified the condemned-convict Shafique who was present then in the accused-dock. He also identified the co-accused Sumon who was also present at that time. The informant in his testimony testified at a stage that the video picture which was within the Close Circuit Camera of his hotel go to show that the accused Shafique, Khokon and Sumon came to his hotel and left his(P.W.1) hotel after the occurrence and the video footage of the Close Circuit Camera was seized by the investigating authority in his presence and he put his signature in the seizure list. The informant identified the seizure list and the signature therein which have been marked as Exhdibit-2 and 2/1 respectively.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">During cross-examination the informant in a reply to a question from the side of the defence admitted that his son Atiqur Rahman used to purchase CD and VCD from the condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique and he (P.W.1) has heard from his driver Alamgir that Atikur Rahman at the time of returning to his residence, was called on by the accused Shafique through mobile phone and getting that mobile call Atique returned back to the hotel and went to the room No.322, which was allotted in the name of the condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique and its number is 322. The informant specifically denied that the accused Shafique because of torture after his arrest gave his confessional statement.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">P.W.2 of the prosecution, Md. Alamgir is a driver by profession and he testified before the Court during his testimony that he is the driver of the informant’s private car and the date of occurrence is on 29.11.2010. On that date he brought the victim Atiqur Rahman at about 9.00 a.m. to his hotel Anurag and at about 2.45 p.m. Atiqur Rahman started to return back to his<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>residence from hotel and when they reached to a place namely ‘Nayarpar’ nearer to ‘Fortune Garden Hotel’, Atiqur Rahman received a phone call and with regard to this P.W.2 testifies as follows: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 27.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><em><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">“</span></em><em><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; line-height: 110%;
