line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>This prosecution witness No.2 Alamgir in the last portion of his examination-in-chief testifies that after the arrest of Shafique, he (P.W.2) has seen him (Shafique) in the RAB camp, where Shafique made a confession that he along with Sumon and Khokon has killed Atiqur Rahman.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">During cross-examination the witness No.2 testified at a stage that at the time of their returning back to the hotel, he asked the victim Atique, who has called him over phone. This witness in his testimony corroborated the prosecution case and denied the suggestion of the defence that he did not enquire into the caller of the phone, who over mobile phone called on Atique. This witness also denied that the accused Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique did not give any phone call to the victim, telling him to come back to the hotel. He also denied that the accused Shafique did not confess his guilt before the RAB.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">P.W.3 Shahabuddin is the Assistant Manager of Hotel Anurag. This witness in his testimony testified that, prior to one year of the occurrence he joined in his post and the date of occurrence is 29.11.2010. On that date he was on duty from 3.00 p.m. and 3/5 minutes prior to that, he found<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Atiqur Rahman to start for his residence, but after 4/5 minutes Atique again come back to the hotel and went to the 2<sup>nd</sup> floor, and about 15/20 minutes to that, this witness observed that one boarder of that hotel ‘Shafique’ along with two others coming out of his room and going outside of the hotel, at which this witness asked him(Shafique) as to whether he will leave or come back to the hotel and in reply<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>to that question, Shafique told him that for bringing money from S.A. Paribahan he is going outside and he wanted to know the location of S.A. Paribahan office from this P.W.3. This witness also in his testimony testified that their General Manager Mahmuduzzaman @ Jewel after 10/15 minutes, coming before him informed that the mobile phone of their junior boss Atiqur Rahman is stopped, and stating that, their<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>G.M. Mahmuduzzaman Jewel started to find out Atique and going in front of room No.322 hearing the sound of shower inside that room on bringing duplicate key, opened that room and same times after that, they informed this witness that their junior boss has been killed. Thereafter, P.W.3 went to the place of occurrence room and found Atique fastened with the ‘sofa’ of that room, tiding neck, waist, hands, legs by rope and the mouth was closed by scotch tape. Finding that occurrence, this witness informed their senior boss over telephone and the G.M. of the hotel informed the police station and RAB through phone. At a stage of deposition, this P.W.3 testifies that, hearing about the arrest of accused Shafique by RAB, they went to the office of RAB and in front of all, Shafique confessed that he along with Sumon and Khokon has killed their junior boss.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">During cross-examination P.W.3 testified at a stage that he has deposed before the police officer sitting in the hotel, but he cannot recollect that date. P.W.3 denied the suggestion that he did not tell anything before the Investigating Officer about his statement in the court. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">P.W.4 Md. Abdul Monim is a seizure list witness. This witness testified before the Court that the date of occurrence is 29.11.2010 and at about 4.09 p.m. he has heard that Atiqur Rahman has been killed in hotel Anurag. In presence of this witness on 01.12.2010 the Investigating Officer from the ground floor of hotel Anurag within office room of the hotel seized the name and address of the assailant, which was written in the hotel register. This witness identified the seizure list and his signature therein which has been marked as Exhibit-3 and 3/1 respectively.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">During cross-examination P.W.4 testified at a stage that Atiqur Rahman was his friend.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">P.W.5 Abul Hasan Babul in his testimony testified that the informant Khorshed Ali happens to be his maternal uncle and the victim Atiqur Rahman is his brother. On 29.11.2010 the occurrence was held and in presence of this witness the police officer prepared the inquest report of the victim Atique. This witness as witness of the inquest report put his signature. He identified the inquest report and his signature therein which has been marked as Exhdibit-4 and 4/1 respectively. This witness also testified that he has heard about the occurrence that in the boarder’s room No.322 of the hotel, accused Shafique along with his accomplices committed the killing and after killing the deceased Atique, they have left the hotel at about 3.00/3.30 p.m. and the two other accomplices of the killer Shafique were Sumon and Khokon.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">28.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">P.W.6 Mahmuduzzaman @ Jewel is the General Manager of Hotel Anurag and in his testimony he has testified about the case of the prosecution and corroborated the ejahar with other prosecution witnesses No.2, 3, 4 and 5. During his deposition P.W.6 the General Manager of the Hotel categorically testified that when he noticed that the mobile phone of their junior boss Atiqur Rahman is switched off, he started searching and at a stage of that, he went in front of room No.322 and heard water falling sound from the closed room No.322 which is under lock and key from outside. Thereafter, bringing duplicate key of that room he opened the room and found their junior boss fastened by a rope with a ‘sofa set’ tiding his hands, legs, waist and neck by that rope and the mouth of the deceased Atique was closed by a scotch tape. Finding that scenario this witness told the driver to inform the owner of the hotel instantly and he informed the RAB and police about the occurrence. After getting his information police and RAB came to the place of occurrence. During his deposition this witness No.6 Jewel testified at a stage that on 01.12.2010 from the office room of the hotel, investigating officer seized the bio-data of the boarder of the place of occurrence room No.322, the condemned-convict Shafique and in his(P.W.6) presence the seizure list which was prepared for that seized <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">alamat</em>(papers), he put his signature. This witness identified the seizure list, his signature and the bio-data of the condemned-convict Shafique which were in two forms and marked as article Exhibit No. I and I/1 respectively. This witness also testified in his testimony that in the video of the CC Camera of that hotel it is found that the co-accused Khokon, and Sumon along with principal accused Shafiqur Rahman is entering into the hotel and going outside of the hotel and the police seized these videos through seizure list which were identified by this witness.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">29.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">During cross-examination this witness categorically testified at a stage that he has appointment letter about his appointment as General Manager of the hotel and his duty was in the hotel from morning to afternoon till 4.00 p.m. and thereafter, from 06.00-11.00 p.m. This witness in a reply to a question from the side of the defence, specifically testified that at the time of occurrence the Managers were Salauddin and Sahabuddin, and they were on duty also.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">30.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">P.W.7 Md. Salauddin corroborated the witness No.06 in toto and clearly testified before the trial court that he was on duty from 3.00 p.m., and 20-25 minutes after his joining in the duty, he found the friend of their junior boss Atique namely Shafique and two others are going outside from the hotel. Finding them, this witness and his co-manager asked Shafique as to where they are going and in reply, Shafique told that they are going outside for bringing money from S.A. Paribahan. This witness in his testimony corroborated the prosecution case and also identified the accused Shafique in the accused-dock.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">31.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">P.W.8 Moloy Dutta Mithu is a hear-say witness of this case. This witness has heard about the occurrence and in his presence the inquest report was prepared. As witness of the inquest report he gave his signature therein and besides this; in his presence the material exhibits i.e. the rope, the tiger drink bottle, the bad-sheet, scotch tape, CD cover, one undervest and two bags were seized by police. The sofa set was also seized and a seizure list was prepared and as witness this P.W.8 gave his signature therein.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">32.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">P.W.9 Sumon Chakraborty is another inquest report witness. This witness in his testimony testified that the deceased Atiqur Rahman Atique supervised the Hotel and on 29.11.2010 at about 3.00 p.m. while he was on duty in the nearby Chinese Restaurant belonging to the same owner, the informant of this case, at about 3.30 p.m. the General Manager of Hotel Anurag with other staffs went to his(P.W.9) restaurant for searching their junior boss Atique. Hearing about the occurrence, thereafter this witness went to the place of occurrence and in his presence the inquest report of the dead body was prepared by police.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">33.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">P.W.10 Shamsul Islam is a hotel boy of Hotel Anurag. This witness testified in his testimony that, since 2004 he is serving as hotel boy in the hotel and Atiqur Rahman @<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Atique was their junior boss and the condemned-convict Shafique was known to him (this witness) since he(Shafique) came to their hotel frequently prior to the occurrence. P.W.10 also testified that, 5/6 days prior to the occurrence, Shafique coming to their hotel became the boarder of room No.322, and on 29.11.2010 two guest of Shafique came to his room and stayed there till afternoon and at about 3.30 p.m. all the three accused jointly came out of the room and went outside, and subsequent to that, finding their junior boss no where they started searching and went to the 2<sup>nd</sup> floor of the hotel and in front of room No.322 they have heard sound of water falling and the room is under lock and key from outside. Thereafter, by duplicate key opening the door of the room they found their junior boss Atique, but his waist, hands, legs and neck were tide by a rope and the body was fastened with the sofa-set and his mouth was also closed by scotch tape and Atique was senseless and sent to Osmani Medical College Hospital, wherefrom the doctor told that he is dead.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">34.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">During cross-examination the P.W.10 hotel boy Shamsul Islam testified at a stage that in the 2<sup>nd</sup> floor there are 25 rooms and 3 hotel boys were on duty at that time and Mizan was one of them.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">35.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">P.W.11 of this case, Md. Badrul Islam in his deposition testified that the victim Atiqur Rahman @ Atique happens to be his cousin’s husband.On the date of occurrence at about 4.00 p.m. the father of the victim Khorshed Mia informed him that Atique has been killed and knowing about that, this witness rushed to the place of occurrence Hotel Anurag and found the body of the deceased Atique fastened with rope with a sofa-set tiding the hands, neck, waist and legs by that rope and the mouth is closed by a scotch tape. Atique was sent to Osmani Medical College Hospital wherefrom the doctor declared him dead and from 9.00/9.30 p.m. when this witness was in the residence of Atique, at about 1.00/1.30 a.m., a phone call came from a person which was attended by this witness, and at that time, that person disclosing him as a friend of Atique inquired about Atique as to whether he is alive and that number was ‘01725206307’. This witness tried to know the identity of the caller but the caller disconnected the phone. Thereafter, this witness gave the number of that phone to everybody including the members of RAB and police and one hotel boy informed that the accused Shafique use that phone number and that number was given by Shafique to that hotel boy 2/3 time to flexi load. This witness also testified at a stage that after apprehension of Shafique he confessed his guilt in killing the victim before RAB, reporters and all of them and Shafique also disclosed the names of his accomplices namely Sumon and Khokon.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">36.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">P.W.12 Most. Rejia Begum is the mother of victim Atique. She has corroborated her husband, the informant of this case Hajee Md. Khorshed Ali and also deposed that in their presence the accused Shafique disclosed before RAB that he along with Sumon and Khokon killed the victim Atique for want of money.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">37.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">P.W. 13 Tahmina Rahman is the wife of victim Atiqur Rahman Atique. She also corroborated the other witnesses and testified about the extra-judicial confession by the condemned-convict Shafique before RAB and reporters.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">38.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">P.W. 14 is Doctor Abul Monsur. This witness in his testimony testified that he held the postmortem of the dead body of Atiqur Rahman Atique and during his examination he found the following injuries: “<em>Complete circular ligature in the mid level of neck found. Circular Ligature mark on both wrists joint which was found abraded in right wrist. Ligature mark on both forelegs found. Marks of contusion on the both lips found. Incisor teethes of both jaw found displaced</em>.” About the cause of death the doctor gave his opinion in the following way, “<em>Considering autopsy findings and the inquest report, I am with the opinion that, the death of Atiqur Rahman Atiq was due to violent Asphyxia, resulting from strangulation, which was ante-mortem and Homicidal in nature”</em>. This witness identified the postmortem report and his signature therein which have been marked as Exhibit-6 and 6/1 respectively.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">39.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">P.W.15 Sub-Inspector Abdul Alim is the 2<sup>nd</sup> investigating officer of this case. This witness testified in support of his investigation and clearly testifies at a stage that his previous investigating officer Sub-Inspector Khasrul Alam Badal due to his transfer handed over the case docket for investigation to him on 04.02.2011 and taking investigation of this case he went to the place of occurrence and seized the video footage of Close Circuit Camera of the place of occurrence hotel, the duplicate key of the place of occurrence room, the wearing apparels of the victim and prepared seizure list. This witness identified the seizure list and his signature therein which has been marked as Exhibit-7 and 7/1 respectively. This witness also testified that during his investigation he examined the witnesses and recorded their statements and the accused Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique confessed his guilt and this witness produced him before a learned Magistrate for recording his confessional statement. Thereafter, while the charge was proved against all the three accused-persons, this witness submitted charge-sheet against Shafique, Sumon and Khokon under section 302/34 of the Penal Code. The P.W.15 also testified that his previous I.O. Khashrul Alam during his investigation seized some ‘<em>alamats’</em> of the case i.e. the rope made of jute, the bloodstained handkerchief, the bed-sheet, the bloodstain undervest, the pillow cover, scotch tape, different CD and VCD through seizure list and also seized the mobile number ‘01752063087’.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">40.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">P.W.16 is a Magistrate, 1<sup>st</sup> Class, Md. Shahabuddin Masum. This witness in his testimony testified that on 15.02.2011 as Senior Judicial Magistrate he was working at Sylhet and recorded the confessional statement of the accused Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique under section 164 of the Code of Criminal Procedure and he has complied with the provisions laid down in section 164 and 364 of the Code of Criminal Procedure and after observing all the legal formalities he has filled up the HCB form ‘M-84’. This witness identified the confessional statement and six signatures which have been marked as Exhibit-11 and 11/1-11/6. The learned Magistrate also testified that the confessional statement was read over and explained to the accused person and admitting that true and voluntary, the accused gave his three signatures therein.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">41.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">During cross-examination from the side of defence the witness No.16, the learned Magistrate categorically testified before the trial court that three hours time was given to the accused for his reflection and he was in his court chamber for that time and he(P.W.16) observed the accused Shafique but did not find any mark of injury or violence in his person and the learned Magistrate also assured the accused that he will not send back to police and he will be sent to the jail custody. This witness denied the suggestion of the defence that the confession is the product of torture by police.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">42.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The last witness of this case, the witness No.17 is the 1<sup>st</sup> investigation officer, Sub-inspector Khashrul Alam Badol. This witness in his testimony testified that during his investigation he went to the place of occurrence and prepared the sketch map, index etc. and also prepared the inquest report of the dead body and seized the <em>alamats</em> including 46 cubits long rope, one bloodstained handkerchief, one bed-sheet, one undervest , two pillow covers and a scotch tape through a seizure list. He also seized some VCD, an old bag, and one royal tiger drinks plastic bottle. This witness identified the seizure list and signature therein and also identified the materials, which were seized by him during his investigation and all these material exhibits have been marked as material Exhibits-II series.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">43.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">On meticulous consideration of the evidences on record along with the case record and scanning the material exhibits including the medical examination report, FIR, inquest report and the confessional statement of the condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique, it transpires that the series of evidences as adduced from the side of the prosecution, has corroborated one another as to the link of this case and the learned Magistrate who recorded the confessional statement of the principal accused the condemned-convict Shafique, during recording of the statement strictly complied with the provisions laid down in section 164 and 364 of the Code of Criminal Procedure and it was clearly explained to the accused before recording of his confessional statement that, (i) the learned Magistrate is not an officer of police but a Magistrate; (ii) that he is not bound to make a confession; (iii) that if does make a confession it may be used in evidence against him; (iv) that he should not say anything because others have told him to say it but is at liberty to say whatever he really desires to say; (v) that he should say nothing which is untrue.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">44.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Apart from this, there is a clear declaration of the learned Magistrate to the effect that the confession was voluntarily made and it is true. In this context; in the case of <em>ABM Nazmus Sakib Ashik –vs.- State</em>, 12 BLC (AD) 203 our Apex Court held, the Magistrate appears to have recorded his satisfaction as to the voluntariness and spontaneous nature of the confession of the accused. It appears that the confession has not been vitiated by any illegality. Besides, this Court in the case of <em>Abul Hossain –vs.- State</em>, 46 DLR 77 opined that the provisions under sections 164 and 364 of the Code of Criminal Procedure are mandatory and required to be strictly followed to make the confession voluntary and true and fit for reliance for convicting the accused on his confession. In the case of <em>Nausher Ali Sarder –Vs.- The State</em>, 39 DLR (AD) 194, their lordships held that the surrounding circumstances are ordinarily the only material from which the inference of a confession may be drawn. Confession when proved against the confessing accused, it can be taken into consideration against co-accused in the same offence.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">45.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Having regard to the facts, circumstances and the discussions referred to above, we are constrained to hold such a view that here in this case it is proved beyond all shadow of doubt by series of cogent evidence that the condemned-convict Shafique is directly involved with the offence of killing the victim Atiqur Rahman Atique. We also find that the learned trial court in fact during examination of the convicted-appellant<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Suman @ mama Suman under section 342 of the Code of Criminal Procedure complied with the provisions by giving attention of the accused to the incriminating evidences which were produced against him and as such no illegality or irregularity is noticed by which it can be held that the convicted persons have been prejudiced or has been deprived of getting justice from the learned Metropolitan Sessions Judge, Sylhet.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">46.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Furthermore, obviously we have every reason to draw such inference that there was no ambiguity or confusion<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>in the mind of the accused before giving reply to the question put before him by the learned trial court and in view of the facts and circumstances of the case we are of the considered view that the learned Metropolitan Sessions Judge, Sylhet during deciding the fate of the case in favour of the prosecution committed no such infirmity by dint of which the impugned judgment and order of conviction and sentence of death can be interfered with. Moreover, it is observed that the learned trial court rightly considered the case in its true perspective.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">47.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Having gone through the evidences on record we find on our anxious consideration over the testimonies of the ocular witnesses, who personally witnessed the convicted persons immediately after the occurrence at the time of their leaving the place of occurrence hotel and being satisfied on the assessment of the evidences by the trial court in its total approach, we are inclined to hold such a view that the trial court committed no wrong. Moreover, the ingredients of the offence as we have spelt out were also duly appreciated by the learned trial court and as such in the discussions made above particularly the nature of the offence and the confession of the principal accused as to the implication and participation of the convicts in the heinous crime of killing the victim Atiqur Rahman Atique, we are of the view that the prosecution has been able to prove the case beyond all shadow of doubt and as such the impugned judgment and order of conviction and sentence should be sustained.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">48.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Considering the facts and circumstances of the case it is crystal clear from the factual aspects, that the condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique with the previous intention to murder the victim Atiqur Rahman Atique which was pre-meditative, under the ambit of section 300 of the Penal Code committed the murder. As such we find nothing in the circumstances of the case and the conduct of the condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman to take lenient view in the matter of sentence despite our best concern to temper justice with mercy. Considering all aspect of the matter we are obliged to the law to sustain the order of conviction and sentence.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">49.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Before parting, however, we must observe that the circumstantial evidences which are evident from the face of the records are cogent and despite in the instant case there is no direct eye witness of the occurrence, the circumstantial evidence as it appears is trustworthy, tangible and credible, and hence, it cannot be ignored and definitely the circumstances makes it clear that the absconding condemned-convict and his accomplices the appellant Sumon @ Mama Sumon and Khokon are directly involved in the occurrence of killing the victim Atique and under section 8 of the Evidence Act, 1872 the abscondence of the condemned-convict and Sumon after misusing the bail privilege being on guilty conscience, is a strong corroboration to the prosecution case that they are the culprits. The extra-judicial confession which is transpires from the testimony of the witnesses, are also a corroboration of the prosecution case as well as the confession made by the confessing condemned-convict Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">50.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Be that as it may, we are inclined to hold such a conclusion that the argument advanced from the side of the learned Deputy Attorney General Mr. Md. Aminul Islam is consistent with the case record and as such these are well founded.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">51.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">In the result, the Death Reference No.78 of 2014 is accepted and consequently, the Criminal Appeal No.3378 of 2015 be dismissed.</span><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN-AU; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> The impugned judgment and order of conviction and sentence dated 12.11.2014 awarded by the learned Metropolitan Sessions Judge, Sylhet in Sessions Case No.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">1808 of 2013 (previous Sessions Case No.736 of 2012) is hereby upheld and confirmed.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN-AU; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">52.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN-AU; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Let the Death Sentence of the condemned-convict namely </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Md. Shafiqur Rahman @ Shafique (absconding), son of Hazi Rahmat Ullah, 28 Ganaktuli Lane, Police Station-Hazaribag, Dhaka, be executed after his arrest/surrender in accordance with law and the judgment and order of conviction and sentence passed by the learned Metropolitan Sessions Judge, Sylhet in </span><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN-AU; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Sessions Case No.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">1808 of 2013 (previous Sessions Case No.736 of 2012) in respect of the remaining convict-appellant Sumon @ mama Sumon is affirmed.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Abdul Hamid and another</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Accused-respondents</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> </span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Sections 173 and 241 </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Although the informant made allegation under sections 10, 30 of the Ain, 2000 but the police during investigation tried to collect evidence to that effect. But none of the local witnesses supported the allegations made by the informant. Therefore the police submitted final report. On receipt of the police report the learned Judge of the Tribunal after considering the materials on record rightly discharged the accused. It is pertinent to point out that challenging the police report the informant did not file any narajee petition to that effect. Therefore, we are at one with the learned Judge of the Tribunal. Thus the appeal having no merit fails.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">      </span>...(11)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 8.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">No one appears</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: right; line-height: 110%;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">For Informant-appellant</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">No one appears</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: right; line-height: 110%;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Accused-respondent nos.1-2</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mrs. Sakila Rowshan, D.A.G. with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mrs. Sharmina Haque, A.A.G. and</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> Md.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> Showardhi, A.A.G.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">For the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>State-respondent no.3.</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="text-decoration: none;"> </span></span></u></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="text-decoration: none;"> </span></span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Syed Md. Ziaul Karim, J. </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">By this appeal, the informant-appellant has challenged the legality and propriety of the order dated 18-06-2001 passed by the learned Judge of Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Daman Bishes Tribunal, Habigonj (briefly as Tribunal) accepting the Police report and directing to prosecute the informant under section 17 of the Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Daman Ain, 2000(briefly as Ain 2000)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Facts in brief, are that on 07-11-2000 the appellant as complainant filed a petition of complaint in the Court of Magistrate, First Class, Habigonj against the accused respondents alleging that on 14-10-2000 the accused respondents forcibly entered into the dwelling hut of the informant and attempted to abduct his daughter Minara Begum failing which the accused assaulted the victim. With this allegations the complainant filed the instant case.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On receipt of the complaint the learned Magistrate referred the case to the local Police Station wherein it was recorded as Habigonj P.S. Case no. 07 dated 05-01-2001 under Sections 10, 30<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>of the Ain, 2000.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Police after investigation submitted final report in favour of the accused respondents and sought for permission to prosecute the informant under section 17 of the Ain, 2000. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On receipt of the Police report the learned Magistrate referred the case to the Tribunal wherein the learned Judge by the impugned order dated 18-06-2000 accepted the Police report and discharged the accused and also permitted to prosecute the respondents under Section 17 of the Ain,2000.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Feeling aggrieved the informant preferred the instant appeal.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">No one appears on behalf of the appellant to support the appeal. In view of the facts this is an old appeal of 2001 we are inclined to take it up for disposal on merit considering the materials on record.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">No one appears on behalf of the accused-respondent nos.1-2 to oppose the appeal.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Deputy Attorney General appearing for the State-respondent no.3 supports the appeal and submits that the learned Judge of the Tribunal after considering the materials on record rightly accepted the Police report and discharged the accused which calls for no interference by this Court.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In order to appreciate her submissions we have gone through the record and given our anxious consideration to her submissions.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On going to the materials on record, it transpires that although the informant made allegation under sections 10, 30 of the Ain, 2000 but the Police during investigation tried to collect evidence to that effect. But none of the local witnesses supported the allegations made by the informant. Therefore the Police submitted final report. On receipt of the Police report the learned Judge of the Tribunal after considering the materials on record rightly discharged the accused. It is pertinent to point out that challenging the Police report the informant did not file any narajee petition to that effect. Therefore, we are at one with the learned Judge of the Tribunal. Thus the appeal having no merit fails.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of foregoing narrative, the appeal is dismissed. The order of stay granted earlier stands vacated.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Office is directed to send down the record (if arrived) or to communicate the order at once.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///C:/Users/Hp/Downloads/masum/Issue_January_2020(1)%201/Issue%20__January__2020(1)_Cr.%20A.%20No.2469%20of%202001_Md.%20Ziaul%20Karim,%20J.__4.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;
